Important News

Development of the Battle on the Pinghan Railway Line

Distribution of the Fifth Column

He and Liu Serve as Commanders

The battle on the Pinghan Railway Line: Since the Central Army established contact with the Longhai front, the situation has gradually unfolded, and the attack began on the 11th. Initially, after the Central Army captured Jinan, the Longhai line also took advantage of the momentum to advance. The Pinghan line is a key area for both sides to compete for victory. Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek has visited Luohe twice to inspect the front line and deliberate on the situation. He decided to adopt a new strategy to change the deployment of the army on that road, dividing it into five columns and a central column, with Liu Zhi and He Chengjun serving as commanders. Before the 11th, they had all separately completed their concentration. After the 11th, the entire line was mobilized. Except for the central route, where progress was slightly delayed due to military relations, both the left and right wings made rapid progress. According to successive reports of victory from the headquarters, the first column has captured Fugou, and Liu Guitang's troops have been completely disarmed. Zheng Dazhang and Sun Lianzhong's troops have also suffered extremely heavy losses. This column is now advancing towards Kaifeng. The second, third, and fourth columns are stationed in Xihua, Lingying, and Xiangcheng, advancing towards Xuchang, Xinzheng, Zhengzhou, Rongyang, and Gongxian. Feng Yuxiang's troops Deng Baoshan and Ren Yingqi have also been defeated. The fifth column advanced from the area of Linru, Dengfeng, and Yuxian, approaching Longmen and advancing towards Luoyang. Many of Feng Yuxiang's troops, including Song Zheyuan and Sun Liangcheng, have been disarmed. In addition, most of the first aviation squadron is concentrated on the front, with squadron leader Zhang Yougu dispatching aircraft to Xuchang and Zhengzhou every day to drop bombs. The fifth armored train squadron, the Xiping Minsheng and Lianghao armored trains, commanded by squadron leader Gu Maolin, protects the army along the railway. The Feng Yuxiang army on the left and right wings is trying to defend firmly, and the central route is also taking a defensive posture. Strong fortifications have been built from Xuchang to Zhengzhou, and orders have been issued to all generals not to abandon Zhengzhou unless absolutely necessary. However, with the Central Army surrounding Zhengzhou and Xuchang on the left and right wings, the Zhengzhou and Xuchang area will be difficult to defend. (September 16th)

Committing Hunan Communist Bandits Fleeing Towards the Jiangxi Border

Changsha Correspondence: The communist bandits Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang jointly invaded Hunan this time, launching a major offensive against Changsha. After half a month and seven or eight fierce battles, they were all defeated by the National Army. Zhu De was seriously injured and near death, and there were rumors that Peng Dehuai was also killed by an airplane bombing. Furthermore, their ammunition was running out and food supplies were insufficient (especially salt). The bandits held divergent views and disagreements, and desertions from their ranks increased daily. Starting from the 13th, the bandits began to flee southeast from areas near Changsha. The majority of them advanced along the Zhuzhou-Pingxiang Railway, attacking Liling in an attempt to flee to Pingxiang, Jiangxi. The National Army has dispatched forces to search and advance, and there are no large groups of communist bandits within thirty li of the fortress. Approximately half of the peasants who were coerced have taken the opportunity to escape. The following is an excerpt from the reconnaissance report of the air force team on the 14th, which can provide a glimpse of the situation: (1) Zhang Yuheng and Wu Xingjian, the squadron leaders of the 5th Aviation Team, along with pilots Zhu Hongfei and Yang Xiaolin, flew the Caise No. 3 and Dallas No. 2 aircraft to the Liling area on the afternoon of the 14th to scout the bandit situation. They observed that the bandits who had fled to Longtoupu the previous day were scattered along the lines of Shijiaxia, ​​Meiziyuan, Zhiqianqiao, Fenglinshi, and Huangdazui, fleeing towards Huacaoqiao and Fengshuqiao. Their vanguard had reached Fengshuqiao, while a small detachment split off from Longtoupu and fled towards Zhuzhou, apparently to cover the retreat of the bandits at Fengshuqiao. The planes immediately tracked them and dropped dozens of bombs and incendiary bombs, all of which hit their targets, killing many and littering the roads with corpses. The remaining bandits were terrified and panicked. (2) Qin Zongfan, the squadron leader of the 1st squadron of the 5th Team, and pilot Li Lingyun, flew the Caise No. 4 aircraft from Hankou to the provincial capital on the morning of the 14th. After 3:00 PM, they flew from Xinhae Airport to Fengshuqiao and Liling to inspect the situation. They observed that 30,000 to 40,000 bandits had moved out from Fengshuqiao and were fleeing towards the Jiangxi border. They immediately dropped bombs to attack them fiercely. As the plane moved forward, they saw about 2,000 bandits advancing towards Liling City from Wulipai. The remaining thousands of bandits fled along the Zhuzhou-Pingxiang Railway towards Pingxiang. Their vanguard had reached Fuchongpu and Yingtaoling, moving hastily without stopping. They appeared extremely disorganized. (3) Squadron Leader Zhang Yuheng and others twice flew the Caise No. 3 and Dallas No. 2 aircraft to Yijiawan, Muyunshi, Laodaokou, Langlishi, Dongshan, Baiyanpu, and Tiaomajian to inspect the situation. They found that all areas were quiet and no trace of bandits was found. However, it appeared that a few remnant bandits were lingering in Pujishi, possibly farmers and laborers who had been coerced and were hesitating on the crossroads, wanting to escape from the fiery pit. It is also possible that (4) Squadron Leader Qin Zongfan twice and Squadron Leader Zhang Yuheng three times flew to Liling to continue reconnaissance. They confirmed that there were no bandits north of Longtoupu. The bandits from Fengshuqiao to Yingtaoling were running frantically, one after another. It is said that the bandit party learned that our Jiangxi army had cut off their return route, the provincial capital garrison was preparing to attack, and the central government had dispatched three more divisions to reinforce. The bandits were like ants on a hot pot, suffering from the hardship of having nowhere to go, and had to flee madly to seize the road to escape to their old nest in order to prolong their lives. (5) Squadron Leader Zhang Yuheng flew the Caise No. 3 aircraft to Yijiawan and Tiaomajian on the morning of the 13th to侦炸. He threw multiple incendiary bombs at the location of the bandit military headquarters in Baiyanpu Yangjia Ancestral Hall. He immediately saw the walls of the bandit military headquarters collapsing, the houses catching fire, and the bandits inside fleeing in a chaotic manner. The plane then descended to a low altitude and opened fire with machine guns. Few of those who escaped from the bandit military headquarters survived. The next day, a small vendor selling red peppers came from Dongshan and said that the bandit party was spreading rumors that Peng Dehuai was indeed killed by the bombing of the military headquarters. Therefore, the Red Bandits, upon hearing the news, fled towards Liling in an extremely disorganized manner. (September 15th)

Tang Shengming and Others Again Show Loyalty to He Jian

He Orders Them to Move to Dong'an to Await Orders

Changsha Correspondence: The remnants of the Guangxi clique, including Tang Shengming, Li Zemin, Yan Renyi, and Feng Tianzhu, took advantage of the concentration of the Fourth Route Army in Changsha to suppress bandits and the emptiness of southern Hunan to flee into Hengbin. He Jian immediately dispatched Duan Heng's brigade from Hengzhou to intercept them, and also dispatched Zhang Liangji's brigade of the Sixteenth Division to strike from the side in Baoqing. On the 10th, Qiyang was recaptured, and the pseudo-brigade commander Chen Dunhe and regimental commander Tang Shenghan were killed. Tang Shengming's remnant forces fled towards Yongzhou. Yesterday, Tang and others sent a telegram from Yongzhou to express their loyalty and request that the Fourth Route Army incorporate them. The telegram stated that they only asked that their troops be reorganized into three regiments so that the soldiers would have a place to belong, and that they themselves had no ulterior motives. Whether Tang and others were sincere in this telegram or whether it was a delaying tactic is still unknown. However, for the sake of peace in southern Hunan, He Jian replied in a telegram, allowing Tang and others to withdraw from Yongzhou and move to Dong'an, and then send personnel to the province to discuss the matter. The telegram was signed by Division Commander Tang Shengming, Yan Renyi, Brigade Commander Wang Yi, and Chief of Staff Chen Bishu. Therefore, He Jian's reply was only addressed to Tang and the other four. The text of the telegram is recorded as follows: [Urgent Telegram to Dong'an, Yongzhou to Tang Jifeng (Shengming), Yan Bogang (Renyi), Chen Bishu, and Wang Zhuangbo (Yi), Esteemed Sirs: I have received your telegram with great joy. Previously, you brothers sent several telegrams from Wugang and sent representative Zheng Shaohou to the province with a letter, expressing your unanimous determination to eliminate the communists and not take the opportunity to cause trouble. I replied with praise and entrusted Mr. Zheng to convey my appreciation. Unexpectedly, the ink was not yet dry, the messenger was on the way, and the alarm arrived that Yongqi had fallen and Hengbao was in urgent danger. At that time, our army was fighting a bloody battle with the communist bandits in the suburbs of Changsha. Everyone in the country thought that you brothers were taking advantage of the danger to create chaos and colluding with the communist bandits from afar, blaming He for not taking care of both. Although He loves you brothers, he really cannot but love the local area, and even more cannot but love the people. Therefore, he sent troops from Hengbao to barely defend it. Now, I read your telegram and still say that you have no ulterior motives. He has always treated people with sincerity and is willing to let you brothers realize this as soon as possible. I dare to ask you to quickly lead your troops to retreat to Dong'an and send a suitable person to the province. If He can be responsible for you brothers, he will do his best. A special reply from He Jian with the official seal] (15th)

Establishment of the Hubei Provincial Security Office

Hankou Correspondence: The preparation for the Hubei Provincial Security Office has been underway for a long time. The establishment was delayed due to financial difficulties. After the Three Provinces Pacification Conference, the suppression of bandits and the clearing of villages became the immediate priority. Therefore, Wu Xingya, the director of the office, actively prepared and announced its establishment on the 16th of this month, and began to work. The officials of the office during the preparation period were all appointed by Director He Chengjun and Deputy Director Wu Xingya, including Major General Chief of Staff Zhang Gang, Lieutenant Colonel Secretary Deng Zhi'ou, Major Secretary Shi Wei, Pacification Section Chief Jiang Zuojun, Section Members Wang Chuxiu, Cheng Qi, Wu Changxu, and Hu Daxun, General Affairs Section Chief Lu Yaoxian, Section Members Luo Pingjie, Shan Dawanpeng, Wu Hengjiu, Zeng Chao, and He Zhenjun, and Management Section Chief He Jihua, Section Members Han Jian, Tao Zhidao, and Military Judge Zhong Qi, and dozens of others. In addition, under its jurisdiction are the Four Security Regiments: the Commander of the Second Regiment, Ding Bingquan, the Commander of the Second Regiment, Zhang Michuan, the Commander of the Third Regiment, Wang Shiliu, and the Commander of the Fourth Regiment, Chen Xiping. All of them went to the office on this day to work. Deputy Director Wu Xingya also arrived. On the same day, the official seal was used, and a notice was issued to inform everyone. A telegram was also sent to Director He Chengjun. The telegram read: [Telegram to Commander-in-Chief He, Having Learned of your Arrival in Luohe, The Provincial Security Office has been prepared and started working on the 銑 day of this month. The office address is located in the former Pingtiao Bureau in front of the provincial government. When you return in triumph, we will take the oath of office. Sincerely, Deputy Director Wu Xingya] The organizational charter of the office, totaling seventeen articles, has been approved by the provincial government meeting and is recorded as follows: (Article 1) This province, in order to eliminate bandits and communists and for the convenience of commanding the security regiments, establishes the Hubei Provincial Security Office. (Article 2) This office is under the jurisdiction of the provincial government. (Article 3) This office has one director, who is concurrently the chairman of the provincial government, who commands the security regiments, supervises the officers of this office, and is responsible for suppressing bandits and clearing villages throughout the province. (Article 4) This office has one deputy director, who is concurrently the director of the Department of Civil Affairs, who assists the director in all ongoing matters. (Article 5) This office has one chief of staff who handles all matters of this office under the orders of the director and deputy director, and has the power and responsibility to supervise and command the officers of this office and supervise the implementation of the orders of the security regiments. (Article 6) This office has two secretaries who handle all confidential documents under the orders of the director and deputy director, and the guidance of the chief of staff. (Article 7) This office has two code clerks who are under the command of the secretary and are responsible for translating and sending and receiving incoming and outgoing telegrams. (Article 8) This office has three section chiefs for pacification, general affairs, and management, who handle all matters of their respective sections under the orders of the director and deputy director and the guidance of the chief of staff. (Article 9) The Pacification Section has one section chief, five section members, two clerks, and one scribe.

The responsibilities are as follows: (1) Matters related to education and compilation; (2) Matters related to exercises and reviews; (3) Matters related to promotion and demotion; (4) Matters related to organization and evaluation; (5) Matters related to reconnaissance and investigation of bandit situations in various counties; (6) Matters related to the production and storage of maps. (Article 10) The General Affairs Section has one section chief, six section members, one clerk, and two scribes. The responsibilities are as follows: (1) Matters related to communication; (2) Matters related to the receipt, dispatch, custody of documents, and official seals; (3) Matters related to the arrangement of military discipline, internal affairs, and sanitation within the office; (4) Matters related to the supply of this office; (5) Matters related to the purchase and construction of this office; (6) Matters related to the preparation of salary rosters for this office; (7) Matters related to the management and training of orderlies, messengers, cooks, and employees of this office; (8) Matters related to the feeding and management of horses of this office; (9) Matters related to the equipment and arrangement of meetings and banquets; (10) Matters related to the transmission of orders and notices. (Article 11) The Management Section has one section chief, five section members, one ordnance officer, one technician, one clerk, and two scribes. The responsibilities are as follows: (1) Matters related to the budget and final accounts of this office and its affiliated teams; (2) Matters related to accounting and granting regulations; (3) Matters related to the supply and salary distribution of this office and its affiliated teams; (4) Matters related to the issuance of funds; (5) Matters related to the estimate and calculation of temporary expenses; (6) Matters related to the planning, distribution, storage, and investigation and repair of weapons and ammunition; (7) Matters related to the planning, distribution, and storage of clothing, equipment, food, and utensils. The responsibilities are as follows: (1) Matters related to the interrogation of communist bandits; (2) Matters related to the investigation and handling of crimes committed by officers and soldiers of this office and its affiliated teams; (3) Matters related to the arrest of deserters; (4) Matters related to the prevention of communist bandit riots and the clearing of communist propaganda; (5) Matters related to the registration of the arrest and release of prisoners. (Article 13) This office has one chief military doctor, one military doctor, and one pharmacist, who, under the orders of the director and deputy director and under the command of the chief of staff, are in charge of the diagnosis of this office and the special service brigade, the replenishment and distribution of sanitary materials for the affiliated teams, and the examination of medical personnel. (Article 14) This office has one special service brigade, which is responsible for guarding the office and arresting, guarding, and escorting bandits. (Article 15) The detailed rules of service for this office will be determined separately. (Article 16) If there are any matters not covered in this charter, they may be submitted for amendment at any time. (Article 17) This charter will be implemented after being resolved by the provincial government meeting. (September 16th)

Shandong Province's Finances in the Past Year

Jinan Correspondence: The outgoing Shandong Finance Director Yuan Jiapu recently compiled a general statement of income and expenditure during his term, in the form of a balance sheet of treasury receipts and expenditures, and submitted it to the current Finance Director Wang Xiangrong for acceptance, and presented it to the provincial government and the Ministry of Finance for record. It was found that the total budget revenue for the province's local budget during Yuan's term in the eighteenth year was 23,600,952 yuan, and the total expenditure was 23,592,504 yuan. The revenue listed in Yuan's transfer sheet this time totaled 14,896,817 yuan and one dime and three cents, and the expenditure totaled 15,135,191 yuan and eight dimes, which differed greatly from the budgeted amount. Furthermore, the final account for Yuan's term in the eighteenth year has not been published. Wang Xiangrong is currently ordering the department to check each item in the transfer list to get to the bottom of the matter. The following is a record of the amounts listed in Yuan's transfer sheet to show the financial situation of Shandong Province in the past year. (1) Revenue: In the seventeenth year (May and June of the eighteenth year), a total of 834,622 yuan and four dimes and nine cents was collected from the previous term's transfer and various taxes. In the eighteenth year, the total amount of various taxes collected throughout the year was 14,896,817 yuan and three dimes and one cent. During the period stationed in Qingdao in the nineteenth year, a total of 142,326 yuan and six dimes and eight cents was collected from various taxes. During the period back in Jinan, a total of 1,184,443 yuan and four cents was collected from various taxes. In total, 17,058,209 yuan and five dimes and two cents was collected during his term. (2) Expenditure: In the seventeenth year (May and June of the eighteenth year), a total of 581,070 yuan and three dimes and four cents was paid for military and political expenses. In the eighteenth year, the total amount of military and political expenses paid throughout the year was 15,135,191 yuan and eight dimes. During the period stationed in Qingdao in the nineteenth year, a total of 145,861 yuan and nine cents was paid for military and political expenses. During the period back in Jinan, a total of 1,188,475 yuan and one dime and six cents was paid for military and political expenses. In total, 17,050,598 yuan and three dimes and nine cents was paid during his term. The remaining balance after offsetting the revenue and expenditure was 7,611 yuan and one dime and three cents, which was transferred to the new term. In addition to the bills of exchange and the demobilization treasury bonds used as collateral, only 1,920 yuan and one dime and three cents in cash was actually transferred. (15th)

Guangzhou: Restaurant Closures Still Deadlocked

Three Arrested Restaurateurs Released

Authorities Still Do Not Intend to Revoke Joint Receipt System

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangzhou restaurant industry has been unanimously suspending business since the 6th in protest of the joint receipt system implemented by the donation merchants, awaiting a decision. On that day, a total of more than 250 restaurants were closed in the city. On the second day (the 7th), more than 20 Western restaurants and other establishments joined in. On the third day, even those who specialized in catering without retail storefronts closed their doors one after another. Only five or six flower banquet restaurants in Chentang were not unanimous in suspending business due to special circumstances. However, the strike trend has become unstoppable. In order to maintain contact, the restaurant owners, including Chen Fuchou, the manager of Nanyuan, Lin Ji, the manager of Wenyuan, and Ye Shaogu, the manager of Moshan Pavilion, held a banquet meeting at the Yongchun Lou Yongyu Hall in Chentang at 10:00 PM on the 7th to deal with the donation merchants. Unexpectedly, the matter was not kept secret and was discovered by the donation merchants, who reported to the special task force of the Department of Finance, accusing the restaurateurs of inciting the strike. That evening, the special task force dispatched a team to surround Yongchun Lou and arrested the three men, detaining them at the Department of Finance for interrogation. After Chen, Lin, and Ye were detained, all the restaurant owners who had already suspended business fled, fearing for their safety. They believed that Chen and others were innocent and should not have been arrested arbitrarily. Therefore, each store sent one representative, totaling more than 200 people, to the provincial government at 3:00 PM on the 8th to petition and jointly elect District Someone and others as the five people responsible for meeting with Chen Mingshu, the chairman of the provincial government. Chen was unable to meet due to other business, so he sent Secretary Lei Jiyun to receive the restaurant representatives. The restaurant representatives explained that the restaurant strike was due to the joint receipt system implemented by the donation merchants, which the entire industry considered to be harsh and difficult to implement, and that the unanimous strike was out of public opinion. Now that Chen and others had been suddenly arrested by the Department of Finance, it was unjust, and they requested that they be released to redress the injustice. If the government could immediately revoke the joint receipt system, the restaurant industry would resume business. Secretary Lei promised to convey the situation to the chairman and reassured them before sending the petitioning group away. On the same day, the provincial authorities instructed the Department of Finance to interrogate the three merchants who had been detained and release them after they had given a written guarantee. Around 5:00 PM that evening, the interrogation section of the Department of Finance brought the three men up for interrogation. Each of them strongly denied inciting the strike. The official said that if they had not incited the strike, the restaurant owners related to the detainees should resume business first to show their sincerity. Chen and others immediately agreed and personally provided a written guarantee with their seals, acknowledging the resumption of business. Around 6:00 PM, Chen and others were finally released. Earlier, when the petitioning group returned from the provincial government, they stated that the joint receipt system case would be submitted to the provincial affairs meeting for resolution on the 9th. However, during the 111th meeting on the morning of the 9th, only reports were given, and the joint receipt system case was not included in the agenda. Only Fan Qiwu, the director of the Department of Finance, reported on the handling of the joint receipt system case and explained the reasons for the dispute. The chairman said that now that a strike had occurred, it was best to resolve it as soon as possible. If the restaurant industry was willing to suspend business, the government would only have to wait for them to come to their senses. However, if there were any threats to suspend business, the government would have to deal with them severely. The result of the discussion was that the entire case was still handed over to the Department of Finance for handling. According to sources from the Department of Finance, the financial authorities do not seem to intend to revoke the original plan. Therefore, the restaurant industry plans to petition various agencies again today. (September 10th)

The Turmoil of the Tianjin Customs' Seizure of the Boxer Indemnity

Used to Fund Eight Schools

Gillis Opposes Seizure

Simpson Rashly Seizes Funds

Tianjin Correspondence: After Simpson took over Tianjin Customs on June 16th, a strike broke out on the 21st. The Chang Customs also took similar action. The diplomatic corps attached great importance to this. Later, Simpson handled the matter properly, and the diplomatic corps also understood that the 5% ad valorem tax levied by the Sea Customs and Chang Customs was still remitted to the Inspector General of Customs and did not affect the fund for foreign debts, so they took a wait-and-see attitude and did not intervene. However, the more than 200 Chinese staff members of the Sea Customs were paid monthly by the Inspector General of Customs. Every day, they had almost nothing to do except go to the club to play billiards. Everyone was very anxious. Former Customs Commissioner Bile went to Shanghai to ask the Inspector General of Customs to transfer him to other customs stations. As of now, only four academically excellent people have been transferred, one to Harbin, one to Qingdao, and two to Shanghai. As for the Chang Customs, the strike lasted for two days. After persuasion, all the workers resumed work. Customs Commissioner Bi Luo was dismissed by Yan Xishan, and Ge Jingyou was appointed to replace him. Later, it was found that Ge was in contact with the South, so Ge was transferred to the Taiyuan headquarters as a senior civil servant, and Lu Jinli was appointed to replace him. Time flies, and more than two months have passed. The new customs officers hired by Simpson have been trained and practiced for two months, and everything is on track. Unexpectedly, recently, the Ministry of Education in Nanjing has not paid the expenses of the eight schools in Beiping for several months. Simpson wanted to ingratiate himself with Yan Xishan, so he suggested that 350,000 yuan be withheld from the Tianjin Chang Customs every month to fund the eight schools. Yan immediately agreed and telegraphed Simpson to do so. This happened on September 5th. On the 6th, Simpson telegraphed the Shanghai Inspector General of Customs, stating that the expenses of the eight schools in Beiping were not available, and that he was ordered to allocate 350,000 yuan per month to fund the expenses. If there were any objections, please reply within three days. Otherwise, he would implement the plan as scheduled. Former Deputy Customs Commissioner Gillis received telegrams from the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing and the Shanghai Inspector General of Customs on the morning of the 9th, opposing the seizure of the Tianjin Customs' regular taxes to fund the eight schools. In the afternoon, Gillis visited Simpson. Simpson had gone to Beiping and not returned. He visited again on the morning of the 10th and, on behalf of Nanjing, issued a written warning to Simpson, with strong wording. The main points are translated as follows: (1) Since the abolition of the Sino-Russian Boxer Indemnity Committee, the power to dispose of the Boxer Indemnity is not in the hands of the Inspector General of Customs, but in the hands of the legitimate government of the Republic of China, which is recognized by all countries in the world. It is a fundamental mistake to consult the Inspector General of Customs. (2) The Boxer Protocol stipulates that the indemnity belonging to Russia is paid from the 5% ad valorem tax levied by all Chang Customs (including Tianjin Chang Customs). However, the amount that Tianjin Chang Customs should pay to Russia every month is less than 350,000 yuan. If you want to withhold 350,000 yuan every month, you will have to embezzle the 5% ad valorem tax of the Sea Customs to make up for it. This matter has exceeded the scope of the Boxer Protocol, and you should be held responsible for destroying the customs precedents. (3) According to the Sino-Russian Conference Treaty of 1924, the use of the portion of the Boxer Indemnity returned by Russia is only for the purpose of running Chinese cultural enterprises, and it does not specify that it should be allocated to the expenses of the eight schools in Beiping, nor does it specify the amount. There is no basis for you to withhold 350,000 yuan every month. (4) The 5% ad valorem tax levied by the national customs is not enough to repay foreign debts. Now you want to withhold the Boxer Indemnity from the Chang Customs and infringe on the customs' regular taxes, making the fund for repaying foreign debts even more insufficient. You should be held responsible for shaking the foundation of the foreign debt fund. Simpson also refuted each point the next day: (1) The Inspector General of Customs has no right to dispose of the Russian Boxer Indemnity. I know this well, so the telegram I sent was a notice, not a request for instructions. I am handling the procedures under the order of the Northern government, and there is nothing inappropriate. (2) After the Sino-Japanese War at the end of the Qing Dynasty, China borrowed a lot of money. The regular customs revenue was not enough to repay foreign debts, and there was a monthly difference of more than 2 million. Therefore, it was decided that all the banknote customs (later renamed Chang Customs) within 50 miles of the customs所在地 should be under the jurisdiction of the customs, and all the revenue should be used by the customs to repay foreign debts. If we now forcibly divide them, there is a lack of reason. (3) The decision to allocate the Boxer Indemnity to the expenses of the eight schools every month was made by the Nanjing government. Now that the Nanjing government is not paying the expenses, the Northern government should continue to allocate it in order to maintain the life of education. (4) Whether the national customs revenue is not enough to repay foreign debts is another matter. This time, the monthly deduction of 350,000 yuan from the revenue of the Chang Customs for the expenses of the eight schools will not actually affect the customs' regular taxes. Moreover, I am handling it under orders, and the Northern government is responsible for it. On the 12th, Gillis received another telegram from Nanjing, instructing him to continue to protest. Gillis immediately summoned important officials to discuss the matter. At first, he advocated publishing a notice in Chinese and foreign newspapers to deny Simpson's seizure of customs duties to fund the eight schools. Later, because the advertising fee was too high, he changed to sending the warning letter to Simpson to the major Chinese and foreign newspapers for publication in the form of news. However, most of the Chinese newspapers in the city did not publish it in its original form. Only the English-language North China Star and the Tianjin Times published it. Now the faculty and students of the eight schools are helping Simpson, so Simpson's attitude is very firm. From last Thursday to this Thursday, the regular taxes that the Sea Customs and Chang Customs should have remitted to the Inspector General of Customs, about 300,000 yuan, have been stopped in preparation for allocating them to the expenses of the eight schools next Tuesday. However, although Simpson is　anticipating, he is also very apprehensive, given Gillis' strong attitude, fearing that he will overreact and cause a diplomatic incident. Therefore, he took a train to Beiping on the evening of the 12th to discuss a stable plan with Zhu Hexiang and the faculty of the eight schools. Zhu also declared to the press in Beiping that the expenses of the eight schools in Beiping are paid monthly by the Inspector General of Customs from the Russian Boxer Indemnity, and 350,000 yuan is transferred to the Ministry of Education in Nanjing. Now the ministry has not transferred it for four months, causing the eight schools in Beiping to stop. In order to maintain the life of education in the eight schools, Yan Xishan decided to order the customs to withhold 350,000 yuan every month, and at the same time ask the Inspector General of Customs to transfer an account. The amount withheld in Tianjin is the same as the amount paid by the Inspector General of Customs to the Ministry of Education every month. The payment of foreign debts by the Inspector General of Customs is not affected in any way. It is natural that withholding it in Tianjin will not affect it either. This principle is very clear, etc.

It is also rumored that Gillis asked Jameson, the British Consul General in Tianjin, to stop Simpson from withholding the customs duties. Jameson said that if there is something inappropriate about Tianjin Customs withholding funds, the diplomatic corps should protest and negotiate. The consul is not in a position to intervene before receiving instructions from the British Minister due to his official powers. Judging from the current situation of both sides, Gillis' verbal opposition is more likely to fail, and the North is also apprehensive, fearing that he will alarm foreigners and cause them to intervene, which will inevitably lead to a deadlock and make it impossible to step down. (September 13th)

Large Quantity of Opium Seized on the Beining Railway

Shenyang Correspondence: The Beining Railway had previously uncovered two opium smuggling cases, both within the trains. Unexpectedly, on the 11th of this month, a batch of opium was again seized on Express Train No. 104 departing from Shanhaiguan for Shenyang. It started when a police officer accompanying the train, Officer Wu, noticed three wicker packages boarded from Xingcheng, followed by another three wicker packages boarded from Baimiaozi. All packages had luggage tags, but the wicker packages were suspiciously heavy. When the train arrived at Jin County Station, the police officer immediately reported to the Jin County Police Section Chief, who then had the wicker packages unloaded from the baggage car for public inspection. The packages were found to contain a total of 937 catties of opium. Investigation revealed that Liang Yuguang, the train guard, was involved in the case. Liang and the opium were taken into custody. Telegrams were dispatched to the Beining Railway Bureau, Tianjin General Bureau, and the bureau's Shenyang office. Subsequently, a telegram from Shenyang instructed that Liang and the opium be transported to Shenyang. The Jin County Police Section then dispatched officers on the 12th to escort them to the Beining Railway Bureau's Shenyang office for interrogation. (12th)

Harbin Tram Network Plan

To be completed throughout the city within twelve years

Harbin Correspondence: The Harbin Electric Company, formerly a joint government-business venture, was reorganized this year into the government-run Electric Bureau. The director remains the previous general manager, Li Tieshan, whose management has been quite successful. As a result, both the Japanese Denki K.K. (Electric Joint-Stock Company) and the French Yong Sheng Electric Company have lost their competitive edge. Although North Manchuria (Bei Man) intends to cede its assets to the Electric Bureau, negotiations have repeatedly failed due to significant price differences, and they are still struggling. The electric lighting company on the Daowai Binjiang County border was acquired by the bureau last autumn, and a branch office was established for operation. Thus, the Harbin electric power industry has achieved a unified trend. As for the tramway operated by the bureau, it is currently scheduled to complete the city's tram network within twelve years, constructing one station each year. With Qinjiagang as the center, it will extend in all four directions: Daoli, Daowai, Xiangfang, and Gu Xiangtun New Anbu. The second phase, from Daoli Shitoudao to Daowai Xu Highway, has been delayed because the Dongtie Hengdao Kou culvert has not been repaired. The general plan for each phase is as follows: Phase 1, the main line from Majiagou General Factory to Daoli Police Street and the branch line connecting from Nangang corner to the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau, completed on Double Tenth Day in 1927. Phase 2, adding a double track from Nangang to Majiagou, completed in the spring of 1928. Phase 3, from Nangang Hospital Street intersection to Daowai Zhengyang Street intersection, completed in the winter of 1929. Phase 4, from Daowai Zhengyang Street intersection via Daowai Old Jiangdi to 16th Street, scheduled to be completed by the end of this year. Phase 5, from Majiagou Tongdao Street to Xiangfang, scheduled to be open to traffic in 1931. Phase 6, if the Kan Tieyi eight-station culvert is built, the road from Daoli will be built first; otherwise, the Xiangfang road will be reserved for modification. Phase 7, from Daoli East Police Street, extend west to Paodui Street, enter Xiewen Street, and fold back to Xincheng Avenue intersection, scheduled to be open to traffic in 1933. Phase 8, from Xiewen Street to Xin'anbu, 1934. Phase 9, from the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau to Gu Xiangtun, 1935. Phase 10, from Daowai 16th Street, two lines will go uphill from Jile Temple via Dajing Street to Qiulin, scheduled to be completed in 1936. Phase 11, from Daowai 16th Street, extend east to Binjiang Park, scheduled to be completed in 1937. Phase 12, from Daowai South 16th Street, turn into Taigu Street and enter Nanma Road, scheduled to be completed in 1938. (12th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Transfer of the Water Police Detachment: The first detachment of the first district of the Shanghai Provincial Public Security Water Police was previously stationed in various locations from Minhang, including Tinglin and Zhu Jing. In case of emergencies, they would be dispatched for patrols. Now, gentry and merchants from Jinshan County point out that bandits can easily appear and disappear along the branching waterways of the county. They believe a stationed detachment is necessary for defense. Therefore, they petitioned the provincial authorities to transfer Detachment Leader Fan of the first detachment to Zhu Jing to guard against bandits, and to transfer Gong Guozhen's detachment to Songjiang as a replacement. It is heard that the provincial authorities have approved this and will implement it next month.

Embezzlement in the Ninth District's Rice Sales: Chen Ziwen, the district chief of the ninth district (Little Kunshan) of the county, was tasked with managing the government-subsidized rice sales upon taking office. It has now come to light that embezzlement was discovered in the district, which was confirmed by the Party branch. It was reported at the Bureau of Rice Sales meeting the other day. It is heard that the points of embezzlement discovered include: the subsidized rice sales in the district were stopped on the 25th of last month, and the district chief issued a notice. However, on the 26th, he reported to the Bureau that he had continued to purchase 360 bags of Xian rice. Also, 18 bags of unsold subsidized rice were found hidden in the home of the former Administrative Bureau Chief, Zhu. Another five bags were sold by the district to the Beihuitong Rice Shop in this city, with accounting records to prove it. The rice hidden in Zhu's home has been retrieved and handed over to the Little Kunshan Public Security Sub-Station for safekeeping, pending handling by the county government. In addition, the meeting decided to transfer the case to the county for strict punishment to deter corruption. It is heard that the county government intends to impose a severe punishment to maintain discipline.

Gu Wei-xiong Goes to France to Study Law: Gu Wei-xiong, a native of this county, graduated from Shanghai Law University last year with excellent grades. Desiring to pursue advanced studies, Mr. Gu boarded a ship in Shanghai the other day and set sail for France to study law at the University of Nancy.

The Bandit Ships Left: The day before yesterday afternoon, a large number of bandit ships suddenly sailed into the Jiaodiao Bay area and anchored. The merchants in the town were alarmed and rushed to put up barricades, but were stopped by the bandits, who claimed they were there for fair trading and did not allow police assistance. The bandits on guard carried sharp weapons. After several hours, they cooked their meals, and then raised anchor and sailed away. It is heard that the temporary posting of guards in this city at 5 pm yesterday is also related to this incident.

Fengxian

Reorganization of Zhuangnan Chamber of Commerce Invalid: The recent reorganization of the Zhuanghang and Nanhui chambers of commerce was approved by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. However, the applicable regulations cited at that time treated the reorganization as a re-election, leading to fundamental errors in the procedure. The County Party Branch has raised objections, and in addition to suspending activities, it has been decided at a joint Party-government meeting to convene the old members of the two chambers of commerce together with the county government to reorganize them in a legal manner.

Sixth Sub-Bureau Captures Bandit Leader: The Chief of the Sixth Public Security Sub-Bureau, Chen Xue-zhu, according to reports, is aware that bandit leader Zhou Zixiang, who is related to robbery cases along the Huangpu-Fengnan border, has returned and is planning to cause trouble. The bureau chief led plainclothes police officers to the bandit's lair the other night, captured Zhou, and obtained a confession. He has already been handed over to the judiciary for interrogation.

Bu Te-wu's Wrongful Accusation Exonerated: In the recent case of a revolt by a small number of undesirable elements in the county police force, the county government considered the matter to be of great importance and has transferred the perpetrators to the Shanghai Songhu Garrison Headquarters for review. It was alleged that Bu You-chang, a special agent of the Second Detachment, was involved. However, his colleagues claimed that the allegation was based on the confessions of the arrested Zhou and Meng, who said that Bu was introduced by Squad Leader Mao, but he did not want to appear in person, so everything was handled by Mao. However, Mao claimed that if Bu was involved, why would he need to ask him to represent him? After repeated questioning, he consistently denied it. At the same time, judicial investigation found no other supporting evidence. It is heard that the Garrison Headquarters has sent him back to Fengxian to be placed under temporary custody by the police headquarters pending investigation. Now, the police officers of the team and local people, seeing Bu's correct conduct and his advanced age and declining energy, all vouch for his lack of any wrongdoing. They jointly submitted a petition to the authorities to guarantee his exoneration.

Jiading

Reward for Reporting Illegal Alcohol: Recently, the market has been flooded with illegal alcohol, causing no small amount of harm. Huang Zhenxun, director of the county's tobacco and alcohol monopoly bureau, is offering a reward for reporting illegal alcohol. Anyone who reports and leads to the capture of illegal alcohol sellers will receive a reward of 100 yuan to prevent abuse.

Anonymous Extortion: Tang Zhengzhi, a resident of Futang Bridge in the fifth district, recently received an anonymous threatening letter along with a bullet, demanding 3,000 yuan. After receiving the letter, Tang reported it to the County Public Security Bureau. On the evening of the 5th, he sealed old paper as a money package and sent someone to place it in the graveyard specified by the bandit. At the same time, armed detectives sent by the Public Security Bureau ambushed in the nearby cotton field, waiting for the bandits from sunset until dawn, but saw no movement. The investigation has not yet yielded any clues.

Youth Robbed of Funds: Cheng Anzhi's son, Tongchen, 22 years old, a resident of Anting Town South Street, works as a clerk at Guangxiang Grocery Store in the French Concession of Shanghai. On the afternoon of the 11th, he intended to take the 4:30 Shanghai-Changzhou train home, carrying 112 yuan entrusted to him by his colleagues. When he arrived at the station, the train had already left. While waiting in the waiting room, a Mr. Jia, who seemed familiar, struck up a conversation with him, claiming that he had also gotten off the train at Anting and was feeling bored waiting. He suggested going out for a chat, speaking very earnestly. Tongchen, seeing that he was well-dressed, did not suspect anything and went with him to a restaurant not far from the station. They opened a bottle of wine and talked animatedly. After three cups, he suddenly felt dizzy and lost consciousness. On the morning of the 13th, he regained consciousness slightly and found himself lying on a couch in a room. Mr. Jia was nowhere to be found, and the funds were also missing. An old woman brought him a bowl of noodles. Realizing that he had been robbed, he left in disappointment and took a train back home. He was still extremely tired and his speech was still unclear.

Further News on the Murder Case at the Train Station: In the murder case that occurred at the Anting Station on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway in this county, the county government has taken the station porter Lu Jinzhang into custody for interrogation. The station chief Zhou Dunchen was also implicated. County Magistrate Chen sent a letter to the Railway Administration and dispatched Zhu Shou, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, to facilitate interrogation. The reason the station chief was implicated was based on a prior report from the defense corps requesting the arrest of Qiao (A'er) and Zhou (Peirong). Since the complete arrest of the murderers has not been achieved and the ringleaders are still uncertain, the county government yesterday (the 15th) sought the original letter from the Eighth District Office to clarify the truth. District Chief Zhang has complied with the order and submitted it.

Suzhou

Construction Bureau Approves Demolition of Xuanmiao Temple Screen Wall: The demolition of the screen walls on both sides of the Xuanmiao Temple mountain gate has been a point of contention between conservationists and merchants in the area. It has now been learned that merchants such as Xu Xunru received a Construction Bureau order on the 16th, approving the demolition and issuing palace-style municipal blueprints for reconstruction. After receiving the order yesterday (the 17th), Xu Xunru and others paid a special visit to County Magistrate Huang and Construction Bureau Chief Wei, requesting the start of construction soon to facilitate the project. County Magistrate Huang and Construction Bureau Chief Wei stated that they had not yet received instructions from the Construction Bureau and the provincial government and could not execute the order hastily. Furthermore, the screen wall is temple property and must be demolished by workers hired by Abbot Yan Juecang of Xuanmiao Temple.

Investigation into the Case of False Accusation of Subversion: Lu Chengzhang, Wang Shuzhen, and others from the Tongsheng Paper Mill in Hengmian Town, Nanhui County, owed the shop dozens of yuan for paper and small materials. The shop owner, Wu Haisheng, demanded payment from Lu and Wang. Lu and Wang claimed that they had misrecorded the accounts, leading to a conflict. On the morning of August 12th, when Wu happened to be out of the shop, Shao Kang brought a subversive leaflet and threw it into Tongsheng shop, and then ran to report it to the eighth branch of the public security bureau in charge. The bureau ordered a police officer to go and search for the subversive material and then arrested Wu and interrogated him on suspicion of subversion and transferred him to the county government. After Wu was detained, dozens of shops in the area, including Lu Wansheng, jointly petitioned the county government for his release. The county magistrate, being unwilling to interfere, transferred the case to the county high court the other day. Yesterday, Prosecutor Zhu opened the court for investigation.

Verdict in the Case of Stolen and Sold Kerosene: The Shanghai Texas Oil Company had 600 boxes of Happiness Kerosene stolen in July by boatman Wu Fuyuan, who took them to Suzhou, where Xu Dianyuan, Zhang Jiantang, and others stole and sold them for profit. After investigation by the Public Security Bureau's detective team and the Shui-gong'an third district detectives, Xu Dianyuan, Zhang Jiantang, Wu Fuyuan, and others were apprehended and sent to the Wu County Local Court. The verdict was reached the other day (the 15th). Wu Fuyuan, intending to illegally profit himself, was sentenced to eight months imprisonment and a fine of 100 yuan for jointly appropriating property held in the course of business. Xu Dianyuan and Zhang Jiantang, intending to illegally profit themselves, were sentenced to four months imprisonment and a fine of 100 yuan for jointly appropriating the property of others. Zhang Jiantang was fined an additional 500 yuan.

Committee Member Rewarding Wounded Soldiers Robbed: The evening before last (the 15th), two staff members of the 61st Division's Nanjing Office, Zhong Junxiu and Peng Jiu, arrived in Suzhou from Nanjing. They were carrying over 1,300 yuan in cash to be distributed as rewards to the wounded soldiers of the division at the Maple Bridge 15th Rear Hospital. As it was already late, they decided to distribute the money the next day. However, when they were walking through Phoenix, they were suddenly attacked by more than ten people wielding wooden sticks, who injured Zhong's head and snatched the black leather bag containing the 1,300 yuan in cash. Zhong reported the incident to the Public Security Third Branch, which immediately sent him to Suzhou People's Hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning (the 17th), the leather bag was discovered in the Maple Bridge Hanshan Temple river, and a soldier-like corpse was floating in the river. The local security guard reported it to the local procuratorate, which sent Prosecutor Lü Yihou to inspect the scene. The examination revealed that the skin of the deceased was rotting. The bag contained 100 yuan of the stolen money, a passport of Zhong Junxiu of the 61st Division's Nanjing Office (located in the Liangguang Guild Hall in the capital), and a reward ordinance. The examination revealed that the deceased's skin was decayed. The bag contained two dice, thirty-one copper coins, and eleven small coins. There was also three tokens (1) Zhu Zhengjin, First Division, Second Brigade, First Regiment, Second Battalion, Seventh Company (2) Zhu Zhengjing, 15th Rear Hospital (3) The new token of the 15th Rear Hospital. The hat of the deceased had the cap badge of the First Division, but the corpse had no wounds. At that time, they had informed Hammer, who confirmed that the leather bag was indeed his.

Wuxi

Wounded Soldiers Causing Disturbances: Most residents of Kaiyuan Township in Wuxi County make a living by raising fish. Fish ponds line the area from Xianli Mound along Five Mile Lake to Rong Lane. Recently, groups of three to five wounded soldiers have been bringing equipment to fish in the ponds. The villagers rely on the fish for their livelihood throughout the year, and whenever wounded soldiers arrive, the women and children plead with them, but to little avail. Helpless, they appeal to the district chief, Shi Tang, who forwards the complaint to the county government, but to no avail. Yesterday morning (the 17th), more wounded soldiers arrived in the township to fish, but this time the number swelled to over a hundred. The villagers tried to dissuade them to no effect, and a conflict almost broke out. They reported it to the ninth branch of the public security bureau, which in turn reported it to the county government, the public security bureau, and the military police corps, which sent military police to suppress the situation. The wounded soldiers demanded rewards. After repeated persuasion, a resolution was finally reached. The other day, eight representatives of the wounded soldiers went to the county chamber of commerce to demand rewards. County Magistrate Pan and Public Security Bureau Chief Xu attended the meeting and persuaded them for two hours, finally promising to give them a satisfactory answer within three days. They then dispersed. The county government has telegraphed the provincial civil affairs department to request instructions.

Large Numbers of Refugees Suddenly Arrive in Shitouwan: Yesterday morning, about 300 Jiangbei refugees of all ages, both male and female, suddenly arrived at Shitouwan Town in the 16th District (Wan'anshi). They arrived in several civilian boats and went ashore to demand food from shops and residents. The town's commercial corps, seeing the situation, feared something might happen and immediately came out to maintain order and provide food. The refugees spent the night in the town, and the next day, the commercial corps escorted them towards Wujin.

Old Woman Dies Suddenly at Chong'an Temple: Yesterday, an old woman of about fifty years of age, from the countryside, was walking through Chong'an Temple in the city when she suddenly collapsed and lost consciousness. She died shortly after. The local ward head reported it to the county government, which sent an inspector to the scene. The inspection revealed that she had died of illness. The ward head was ordered to prepare a coffin and bury her in a temporary altar, so that her family could claim the body.

Jiashan

The Case of Gu's Arrest is False: News of the much-circulated arrest of Gu has spread as if it were true. According to Gu's neighbors, the case is entirely false. It is true that a gunboat went to Zou's, and a suspicious Mr. Jia was arrested on the opposite bank, but he was soon released after interrogation. Do-gooders then exaggerated and spread rumors, leading to this unfounded rumor.

Changzhou

County Government Convenes Joint Meeting: The Wujin County Government convened a joint meeting of various agencies and groups on the morning of the 16th due to a budget deficit. The meeting was presided over by County Magistrate Wu, and the following resolutions were made: (1) For the 18th year, the local budget is short 30,000 yuan, and a request will be submitted to the provincial authorities for approval to collect a percentage within the 1% range of the previously set land price of 80 yuan. (2) For the 19th year, responsible personnel will strictly urge the collection of old debts and rectify new revenue for local expenses. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

Warehouse Management Committee Meeting: The County Government convened a Warehouse Management Committee meeting on the afternoon of the 16th. County Magistrate Wu presided over the meeting. After the chairman's report, new officers were elected. Xu Wenjun, He Naiyang, Yue Jun, Xie Jun, and Tu Gongfu were elected as members. It was then decided to reclaim the nursing home's buildings for use as warehouses and granaries. The committee will conduct a thorough investigation to improve the grain stockpiles of each city and village.

Nantong

Defense and Suppression Measures for the Tonghai Bandits: In the area bordering Tong and Hai Counties, large numbers of bandits and smugglers, numbering over a thousand, have gathered near Niu Hong and Da An ports. The provincial security corps is currently coordinating with the warships Bo Xian and Jun He, as well as the water patrol team, to suppress them. The provincial government has telegraphed the Haimen County Government to build a motor road and install military telephones in the shortest possible time to facilitate the defense and suppression efforts of the military and police.

Knife-Wielding Bandits in Taizhou Repelled: Large knife-wielding bandits had been causing trouble in the Huangqiao area of Taizhou. After suppression by the provincial security corps commander Li Changjiang, the bandits have now been subdued. Li has moved on to suppress the bandits in Yancheng and Fuyang.

Yangzhou

Bandits Attempted Robbery at Lotus Bridge: Last night (the 15th) at 10:00 PM, four bandits suddenly pushed open the door and entered the home of Tan Yinglou, resident of No. 7 Lotus Bridge. Intending to commit robbery, they were discovered by Officer Yang of the First Public Security Sub-Station, who immediately led police officers to encircle and arrest them. Nearby merchants also rushed to the scene upon hearing the news. Seeing the situation, the bandits fled in a panic. It is reported that the family only lost two pieces of silver jewelry.

Assault Caused by Jealousy, Request for Inspection: The landlady of a certain clothing store in Daru Fang had been having an affair with her neighbor Xu Baoshan for some time. The landlady recently had a relationship with Bi Songfa, inside Tianyi Pool Bathhouse on this street. When Xu found out, the two fought with each other. After mediation, nothing happened, but Xu Baoshan was still not willing to give up. Yesterday (the 15th) afternoon at 5:00 PM, taking advantage of Bi's absence, he used an iron bar to hit him in the head, causing a large wound. The two then fought to the courthouse, where a prosecutor inspected the wounds and took Xu into custody. He was also immediately sent to the Popular Salvation Hospital in Gengzi Street for treatment. According to the doctor, his brain was severely injured, and it is impossible to say whether he is in danger.

Hangzhou

Execution of Kidnapper Zhu Wencheng: On July 21st, the Zhejiang Provincial Bandit Suppression Command received Zhu Wencheng, a kidnapper, from the Zhejiang Inland River Police Bureau. After interrogation, his guilt was confirmed and he was sentenced to death. The other day, the command handed him over to the Water Police Bureau to be escorted to the scene of the crime in Fuyang for execution.

Long-Distance Telephone Lines between Two Counties Opened: After the Zhejiang Provincial Telephone Bureau dispatched Peng separately to plan the Yongjia branch and the Suichang branch, the personnel went to prepare and by now the Yongjia branch had been established on the fifteenth and opened the telephone line. The Suichang branch was also established on the sixteenth.

They yesterday (the 17th) began operation. The telephone fare is one yuan and three jiao every five minutes from Hangzhou to Yongjia and one yuan and one jiao from Hangzhou to Suichang.

Ningbo

Cixi Public Security Bureau Apprehends Many Bandits: Seeing that robbery cases have been occurring frequently, the Cixi County Public Security Bureau dispatched police detectives to conduct strict inspections of travelers at various inns in the city on the 13th and 14th of this month. As a result, they apprehended robbers Ying A'san, A'er, A'jiao, Zhou Xiaomei, Wang A'er, and other seven bandits related to the robbery of Cai Jiaqiao, Hongjia, Su Feng, and other places at Xiangxing Inn in Lower Heng Street. The haul included thirty to forty pawn tickets, a gold ring, a pair of gold earrings, a watch, and two bundles of women's clothing.

Shangyu

Meixiang's Home Robbed: Xuan Meixiang, a wealthy household in Dingzhai Street, Southern Township, was once kidnapped by bandits in the autumn of the year before last and redeemed for 3,000 yuan. Xuan then closed her doors to guests and lived in seclusion. Unexpectedly, at 10:00 PM the other night, more than ten bandits with a foreign accent arrived again at her home. They ransacked the place for over an hour and stole a lot of red and soft clothing, causing losses of about five or six hundred gold.

Bandit Gang's Attempted Kidnapping Fails: Shen Lanxiu, a farmer from Lihai, Western Township, had a daughter married to a wealthy Zhang family in Yuyao. Recently, due to unrest in the countryside of the county, Shen brought her son and his mother to her home for temporary refuge. Unexpectedly, the bandit gang discovered this and gathered eight or nine people with flashlights and pistols at midnight the other day to knock on Shen's door. They falsely claimed that her father-in-law was seriously ill and they were ordered to pick up his mother and son. Shen, suspecting something was wrong in the middle of the night, did not open the door at first. Peeking through the crack in the door, she recognized them as bandits. Shen's mother quickly hid her grandson in the cotton industry outside the back door. The bandit gang broke down the door, forced their way in, and searched wantonly without success, before leaving in disappointment.

Letters to the Editor

Lawyer Zhou Jia of Jiaxing's Letter

To the respected editor, after reading the article titled "Problems with the Succession of the Lu Family of Pinghu" in the Local Correspondence section of your newspaper on September 13 of this year, it is quite inconsistent with the facts. My aunt Lu Zhou passed away with a will that bequeathed her property to her daughter Lu Yulin. The will was used as evidence. On the 11th of this month, Lu Zhou was buried and then Lu Lanbo colluded with Lu Chengqing to forcefully inherit, in an attempt to seize property. My lawyer acted in good faith and Lu Lanbo was at a loss for words. I present the actual situation at the time. Inheritance is a mandatory regulation and does not allow the parties to change it with their will. So can it be forcefully continued if the goal is to seize the property? A lawsuit has been filed and should wait for the legal solution. There is no need to defend ourselves. We are afraid of rumors and hereby write to request that your newspaper publish this letter in the "Letters to the Editor" section for clarity. Zhou Jia, Lawyer, September 16

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Orders Primary Schools

To Perform No More Than Twice a Year

And orders publishing houses to add the New System of Measurement to Arithmetic textbooks

Nanjing, September 17th: The Ministry of Education issued a circular to all publishing houses that future arithmetic textbooks should adopt the new system of weights and measures. Published textbooks should be supplemented with loose-leaf teaching materials for remediation. Furthermore, in light of the prevalent practice of primary schools performing song and dance dramas, which interferes with regular classes, the Ministry issued a special circular restricting each school to no more than two performances per year.

The Central Executive Committee, based on the suggestions of the Special Party Branches of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways, has approved the Ministry of Education to review the issue of songs, dances, and dramas taught in primary and secondary schools being suitable for physical education without interfering with regular classes.

Education Ministry Order for the Adoption of Reviewed Books

The Ministry of Education has issued an order stating that all books reviewed and approved by the Ministry may be freely adopted. Local educational administrative organs may not make separate selections or request the adoption of books based on submissions from publishing houses. Special instructions have been issued to the educational departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities. Upon investigation, it has been found that the review of educational textbooks should be handled uniformly by the Ministry. Previous orders from the former University Council and the Ministry have been issued and recorded. Recently, it has been found that some local educational administrative organs are still independently selecting textbooks and ordering schools to adopt them, which clearly contradicts previous orders. Furthermore, some are hastily ordering schools to adopt books based solely on eloquent submissions from publishing houses, even including books that have not been reviewed, without making any distinctions. Such violations of the order are highly inappropriate. The Ministry hereby reiterates its intentions regarding the review of educational textbooks as follows: All educational textbooks reviewed and approved by the Ministry and the former University Council, as well as those permitted for publication, have been successively published in the Ministry's and the former University Council's official gazettes. Educational administrative organs of all provinces and cities should pay attention to copying and distributing these to all schools so that the schools can freely adopt them. They must not organize review committees or the like to make selections. Schools must not be ordered to adopt specific books. If any publishing houses submit requests for the adoption of certain educational textbooks, these should be strictly rejected and not used as a basis for issuing orders, in order to prevent encroachment and the creation of malpractices. In addition to separate orders, this order is issued for compliance by the relevant departments.

China Economic Society Annual Meeting to Open the Day After Tomorrow

Cai Yuanpei Scheduled to Work and Visit Wuxi

Members Continue to Register

The seventh annual meeting of the China Economic Society will be held in Wuxi starting on the 20th of this month. The news has been reported in this newspaper. Further details are recorded below:

Cai Yuanpei's Visit to Wuxi Scheduled: For the first day of the Society's annual meeting, Cai Yuanpei, Dai Jitao, and Shao Yuanchong were originally invited to give keynote speeches. However, due to Mr. Cai's trip to Qingdao, it was feared that he would not be able to arrive in Wuxi in time. Therefore, the scheduled speaking time was allocated to Mr. Dai and Mr. Shao, who were asked to speak for an additional 15 to 30 minutes each. Now, the Society has received a telegram from Mr. Cai in Qingdao confirming that he will depart on the 19th and arrive in Wuxi on the 22nd. At that time, Mr. Cai will be invited to speak during the meeting. In addition, Shanghai industrial magnate Liu Hongsheng will also attend and speak.

Continued Registration of Members: As of the 15th, more members have registered, including Ren Enhao of the Shanghai National Tariff Commission, Shi Weihuan of the Training Department of the Central Party Headquarters, and Dong Shijin of Beiping, bringing the total number of registered members to 117, with 76 family members.

Meeting of the Preparatory and Reception Committees: The Preparatory Committee has added Yang Hanxi, Jiang Daoshan, and Xu Shouyi as reception committee members. A joint meeting of the Preparatory and Reception Committees was held yesterday at 4:00 PM to discuss and decide on all reception matters. The schedule of station reception times has been printed and distributed to all reception committee members.

Station Reception Times: Trains from Shanghai arrive in Wuxi at 10:28 AM (Early Express), 12:05 PM (Special Express), 3:58 PM (Middle Express), and 5:51 PM (United Hangzhou Special Express). The Night Express arrives at 2:28 AM. Trains from Nanyang arrive at 12:48 PM (Early Express), 1:58 PM (United Transport Special Express), 6:03 PM (Middle Express), and 9:01 PM (Special Express). The Night Express arrives at 3:40 AM. Receptionists will be present to greet passengers from the above trains arriving in Wuxi. No reception will be provided for other trains arriving in Wuxi. Members are advised to take note.

Reception by Educational Organizations: The Jiangsu Provincial Wuxi Education Institute, the Provincial Xizhong Elementary School, the Education Bureau, the Education Association, the County Girls' Middle School, the Junior Middle School, the Private Xizhong School, the Furen Middle School, and the National Studies College, recognizing the great contributions of the Society's members to the improvement of China's economy, and in order to enhance academic exchange and emotional connection, jointly designated representatives from the above organizations to hold a welcome reception at the Provincial Xizhong School. Tu Kaiyu, President of the Education Institute, chaired the meeting and decided to hold a banquet for the Society's members at the Wuxi Hotel or the Daxin Building on the 22nd. Gao Jiansi, President of the Education Institute, will deliver a welcome speech.

Recent Situation of West China Union University

West China Union University, a church university located outside the South Gate of Chengdu, Sichuan, was established by five church groups: the American Methodist Episcopal Church, the English Methodist Church, the Friends Church, the Baptist Church, and the Anglican Church. The entire campus covers approximately 1,000 acres and includes specialized classrooms and a library for the faculties of arts, sciences, medicine, dentistry, and education. The various buildings are exceptionally magnificent and adopt a Chinese palace style, similar to the campus of Yenching University in the East. Founded 20 years ago, it is located in a remote area, so it is less well-known. More than 200 students have graduated. Medical and dental students have made significant contributions to the three southwestern provinces. Each church has its own athletic field, and all five churches share a common athletic field. Students practice diligently on weekdays, so physical education is well-developed, and the university often holds the leading position in the province's sports circles. The principal, Dr. Beech, an American, founded the university single-handedly and endured many hardships. Recently, due to fundraising matters, he returned to the United States. Principal Zhang Linggao is handling affairs effectively and is currently working hard on the registration issue. There are currently more than 500 students, including 50 female students. The school atmosphere is quite pure and rarely interferes with external affairs. Therefore, despite the years of war in Sichuan Province, the school's academic activities have continued uninterrupted. Recently, the school's affairs have been developing increasingly well, so it has attracted a lot of jealousy. Dr. Su Zhepu, a professor at the school, was assassinated on campus. As a precautionary measure, the school built a short wall to enclose it, in order to prevent idlers. However, some people misunderstood this as the school building a fortress for self-defense, which was considered unreasonable, and led a large group of people to demolish the short wall. However, according to the school, the construction of the wall had been approved by the Chengdu authorities.

Local News

Shanghai County Education Association Prepares for Re-election

The Shanghai County Education Association held its tenth executive committee meeting on the 14th of this month at Beiqiao Elementary School, chaired by Zhang Jingye. The most important resolutions included scheduling the re-election meeting for all county members at Tangwan Elementary School at 10:00 AM on September 28th, and sending letters to the County Government, the County Party Headquarters, and the County Education Bureau to send representatives for guidance. In recent days, the executive committee members have been settling accounts and compiling the association's work report for distribution to all members at the meeting.

Expansion of Liangjiang School After Completion of New School Building

The new school building of the Liangjiang Girls' Physical Education School in this city, located on Daji Road, was completed earlier and opened on September 1st, with formal classes starting on the 8th. There are over 300 new and old students. Because this exceeded the projected student enrollment, the new school building was not sufficient for all the programs, and some students were still studying in the old school building on Fangxie Road. Now, three new buildings are being constructed to house a library, the Liangjiang Cooperative, and a storage room. The vacant space behind the school building is the planned location for a gymnasium and ball fields. The architectural drawings for the gymnasium have already been finalized and construction will begin soon. Each classroom will accommodate a maximum of 40 students, so each grade will have two classes. Principal Lu Lihua, recognizing the lack of well-built swimming pools built by Chinese people, which makes swimming a rarity, considers this a major deficiency for a physical education school. He also plans to build a swimming pool in the near future. Mr. Lu believes that the school's current facilities are only part of the ideal and that gradual progress will continue until perfection is achieved.
