Chinese

It is Said the Expedition Football Team Has Returned Home

Heard that they have already left Singapore to return north.

There are two reasons for stopping the trip to Europe.

丨An Explanation for Non-Cooperation with South China丨

The Chinese expedition football team organized by Lehua originally planned to sweep through Southeast Asia and then explore Europe. However, it has recently been rumored that they have returned to the country from Singapore and are already on their way. The Lehua team only had nine basic members. In addition, they invited players from the South China and China teams of Hong Kong to join them to strengthen their team. However, the South China and China sides suddenly went back on their previous agreement and did not cooperate, making things very difficult for Lehua. Moreover, Lehua is a member of the Westerners' Football Club of Shanghai, and the club's charter states that any member wishing to compete in another location must obtain the club's permission. Lehua did not notify the Westerners' Club of this trip abroad, and the Westerners' Club did not give its approval, so the expedition team's trip to Europe was hindered.

South China Team's Explanation

(Singapore Correspondence, August 25th) The fact that the South China players did not join the Chinese expedition football team is worthy of attention from the Chinese sports community. Therefore, the reporter has made many inquiries to inform the people of the country. Last time, there was a conversation from the deputy leader of South China, Mr. Yu Juyan, which was sent to Shanghai in detail, explaining the three reasons for South China's non-participation in the expedition: improper procedures, no economic security, and occupational relations. Readers should still remember this. Therefore, when the expedition team returned to Singapore, the reporter went to the South Sky Hotel where the team was staying to interview Mr. Yu Hengzhi. However, Mr. Yu's intention was that this was a matter of the past and he did not want to say more. At the reporter's insistence, he said that the team was responsible for the expenses of the players. Any player who wanted to return home halfway through the trip could have their deposit refunded. The reason for returning home was not a lack of funds. It was not a question of team members not having enough money to return home. The phrase "occupational suspicion" is even less of a problem. The reporter then asked Mr. Yu Hengzhi, "They borrowed players from South China to join the expedition, but the South China team said that the procedures were not in order. What exactly does that mean?" Mr. Yu said that the expedition team had obtained the consent of Ye Beihua, Li Tiansheng, and Feng Jingxiang in advance, and also sent a letter to the South China Sports Association afterwards. The reporter then asked if he had received a reply. Mr. Yu said that he had not received a reply to this day. As the reporter was about to ask other questions, Guan Jianan, the military doctor accompanying the team, said loudly, "Sir, do you think the Hong Kong players are absolutely brilliant and the Shanghai players are all fools?" The reporter did not ask any more questions and resigned.

However, this simple news could not complete the reporter's draft, so the next morning I visited the team members for a casual chat. Inadvertently, I learned that the South China team members (i.e., the personal opinions of the three gentlemen Ye, Feng, and Li) confirmed that they had agreed to go to Europe before, and even received clothing fees. The reason why Li, Ye, and Feng were unable to go may have been due to the obstruction of the Nanyang Association. The disagreement of opinions in the Chinese sports community is worthy of our research.

Also, when the China team arrived in Singapore the day before yesterday, Chen Guangyao, a member of the expedition team (his home team is the China team), also went to welcome them. The reporter happened to be in the same car with him, so I had a brief conversation with him. I asked Mr. Chen why he and Cao Guicheng were the only ones willing to join the expedition team (because Mr. Chen and Cao were originally one pair in the China team). Mr. Chen said that we should be broad-minded in our work and should not eliminate our personal ambitions because of the relationship with one association. By joining the European trip, I really want to learn more about the world and visit the world, which is a fortunate event in life. The reporter then asked if the expedition team provided any subsidies to the team members on this trip. Mr. Chen said that in addition to travel expenses, we did not receive any money from the team and there were no so-called subsidies, so people should not suspect that we are staff members. You must know that we can participate whenever we want and return whenever we want. We have absolute freedom.

Also, this time when the expedition team returned to Singapore, they did not stay at Hu Wenhu's villa in Banksba Rang because the China team had arrived and it was inconvenient for the two teams to live together, so they stayed on the third floor of the South Sky Hotel, one of the leading Chinese hotels.

There was no special action by the team members that could be reported to the readers, because the weather in Singapore was too hot, so the team members spent most of the day writing letters and working in the hotel, while Zhou Xianyan and Chen Yutian spent the whole day sorting out their photo albums to pass the summer. In the evenings, the team members would go out in groups of two or three to stroll the streets. They didn't have much social contact with the outside world, as the expedition team was no longer new to the area (foreigners now call newly arrived overseas Chinese "new customers").

The team members' meals consist of a breakfast of their choice, with some eating fish porridge or chicken porridge, and others eating noodles. Lunch is served in the hotel, but dinner is eaten at the food stalls under Pearl Hill. This is the only place where Cantonese people sell food. It only opens in the afternoon, and all kinds of roasted pork, sliced boiled chicken, roast duck, and barbecued pork are especially good there. It is economical and delicious, so the expedition team flocks to it. The night before going to Kuala Lumpur, they opened two tables with a total cost of just over five yuan, but the side dishes filled the table. It was a different flavor from what they enjoyed at Hu Wenhu's villa and it was very interesting.

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Sea Guest

Doctor to a sick rich woman: Listen to me, this bottle of medicine must be taken every two hours, one teaspoon each time is enough.

Rich woman: Sir, don't be too economical with me. As long as I get better, spending more money doesn't matter. I want to take it once an hour, one bottle each time. What do you think?

A: Old Bing asked to borrow fifty yuan from me. Do you think he's reliable?

B: As long as he has collateral, you might as well lend it to him.

A: Do you know what collateral he has that I can ask him for?

B: A pair of pants and a rope.

Husband: Oh dear! What should I do? What should I do?

Wife: What's the matter, why are you making such a fuss?

Husband: There's a huge rat in the rice bucket!

Wife: That doesn't matter. Lock it inside and let it starve to death.

Teacher: Children, do you know how the net for playing ping pong is made?

A student: It's made by stringing together many small holes with threads.

Old gentleman: Child, what do you plan to do when you grow up?

Child: I plan to have a son and call him by my father's name so I can beat him up every day.

Strange Tales of Autumn Lamp

— Li Shuping

A few boring tales picked up on an autumn night, recorded urgently for the reference of biologists.

Birds change their habitats due to climate change, often wintering in the tropics and summering in cold regions. In Europe, there is a bird called the "Western Mud Nest" that is produced in Denmark. No one has ever paid attention to its whereabouts when it comes and goes in spring and autumn. Recently, a biologist, wanting to explore how far it migrates, caught countless birds and tied iron rings to their feet before releasing them. Unexpectedly, when winter came, all the ringed birds were found in Sicily and the southernmost part of Africa, a distance of 240,000 kilometers from their hometown. It is the bird that migrates farthest.

The island of Bogoroth is full of volcanoes. Since the explosion, there have been few people there. Recently, a soldier and explorer passed through the area and climbed to the mouth of a volcano to investigate. Suddenly, he found millions of bird eggs in the cave. At first, he was extremely surprised, but upon entering the cave, he felt a warm temperature. Only then did he realize that seabirds were using natural heat to incubate their eggs, which would surely accelerate the process.

Although rats are violent, they are good at knowing the situation. When we design traps to catch them, if a rat falls for the trick, all the rats will flee and dare not approach again. Even more extreme is the fact that there are more rats than people in Aslo, Europe. According to a survey, there are already 6 million rats. They steal and bite, and there is no peace at night for the residents. Recently, a chemical company manufactured 15,000 tons of poisoned bait and planned to pour it all over the city to kill them all. Unexpectedly, two days before the bait was laid, the rats gathered in groups of hundreds and thousands and fled, as if a great disaster was about to befall them. This is also strange.

A hunter in the forests of California recently captured a monster. It looked like a fox with two bat-like wings. It was 40 centimeters long, and its wingspan was one meter. Biologists cannot name it and are currently studying it.

Anecdotes from Chess Competitions

— Pu

For the sake of promoting legitimate entertainment, the Dongtai County People's Education Center held a chess competition this autumn. For a time, 33 people signed up, most of them well-known people, so that there were hundreds of spectators for each game. After three days of fierce battles, Hu Tianmin finally won. The scene of the competition was quite amusing. Recorded here to elicit a smile.

Spectators Form a Screen: The center set up six matches for the preliminary round in the auditorium at 2:00 pm on September 9. Dozens of spectators surrounded each match, forming six natural meat screens. There were even more spectators on the second day of the semi-finals.

Disorderly and Noisy, Spectators Take Over: During the match, spectators would whisper and discuss every move. Then, they would speak and gesture loudly, and the referee had to stop them.

Millions of Sighs and Long Exhalations: There were even more spectators on the third afternoon of the competition. The center drew a large chessboard on the wall of the stage. Lu Xu and Hu Tianmin, who won the right to compete in the finals, played against each other. Every time a piece was moved behind the stage, it was copied on the stage. If they were winning, they would praise each other. If they made a mistake, there would be sighs and exclamations. Although the noise was not very loud, there were no less than three or four hundred spectators in front of the stage, which was almost like a boiling pot. Because they were far from the stage, it did not disturb the players' clear thinking.

Miss He Xiangning's Secretary

— Li Qingduo

Former Central Committee member He Xiangning has long been an important figure in the women's community for her dedication to party and national affairs as a woman. She has sponsored women's movements extensively, hoping to raise women's rights, and has also vigorously promoted women's employment to seek a path for women. Ms. He is skilled in calligraphy and painting, and since leaving Beijing the year before last, she has devoted herself to writing. She has published a collection of her paintings and distributed it to various comrades. Ms. He has a wide circle of friends, and she often engages in correspondence. She especially enjoys writing in her spare time, and she is quite busy with her writing and calligraphy. Therefore, she has hired a female secretary to assist her with everything. I met her at a friend's place yesterday and learned that the female secretary's name is Jin Peiyao, the younger sister of Jin Yanwen, an important figure in the Guangdong naval community. She is a very capable person with excellent literary skills. She has served as a staff member of the Guangzhou Finance Department and the Central Party Headquarters, so she is well-known in political circles as a rare talent in the women's community. It is no small thing for Ms. He's office to have her assistance.

Opening Ceremony of the Weile Garden

— Ji Ping

The Weile Garden opened at 9 p.m. on the 13th. More than 500 Chinese and foreign guests attended the event, and no less than six to seven thousand people from all walks of life came to watch the races. The seats around the perimeter were almost all occupied. The garden owner hosted a grand banquet to entertain the distinguished guests and leaders of the sports community, who were dressed in formal attire and chatting happily. The McInnes military band also came to perform, adding to the elegant atmosphere. After the meal, the competition began with ten events. At that time, the electric lights illuminated the scene as if it were daytime. There were wireless reports of the news in the arena. Seventy-odd jockeys from Chinese, Japanese, and Annamese teams each carried their bicycles and circled the track once, and then competed in order. The result was that the Chinese team won the championship. The speed of the bicycle on the inclined track was extremely fast, traveling at 300 miles per hour, comparable to the speed of an airplane. However, if one is not careful, falling from such a height can easily lead to danger. There was also a motorcycle contest, which was even faster. Flying around the track was dazzling and astonishing.

The garden is located to the left of Haig Road, covering an area of twenty acres. The entrance is a tunnel, and further in is a plaza. In the center is a dance floor, and on both sides are special seats that can accommodate 400 people, furnished with tables and chairs for guests to dine. Around the perimeter is a wooden track shaped like a sycee, about one mile in circumference and two zhang in width. The steepest part forms a 45-degree acute angle, which is quite smooth. Outside the field are four high platforms, each of which can accommodate a thousand people. The entire building is exquisitely grand and was designed by the French architect Taifaner and completed in more than half a year.

According to Weile Garden staff, there are currently more than 300 members, five of whom are of Chinese nationality, and the others are Japanese, Russian, Annamese, and Korean. There are more than 100 people who have received competitive training, and 57 of them are qualified to compete. In addition to bicycle and motorcycle races, the scheduled performance types also include Jai Alai, Chinese boxing, handball, and dancing, but bicycle races are its main purpose. Famous bicycle manufacturers from the United States, France, and Austria use this to promote the sturdiness and durability of their bicycles and expand their sales. Therefore, merchants in Shanghai who operate this business are more enthusiastic about bicycle races. It can be said that foreigners' efforts to compete in trade with China are profound and far-reaching.

Ramblings on Peking Opera

— Meilang

Peking Opera is named because the old capital was its place of origin, hence the name "Jing" (Peking) opera. However, since the political reforms and the relocation of the national capital to the south, this name has been abolished. It would be more appropriate to change the name to "Ping" (Beijing) opera, following the example of renaming Beiping. However, that sounds too awkward and does not flow well. As for calling it "national opera," there are many types of opera in our country, so using this one term to encompass all the others seems somewhat inaccurate.

Chen Delin, the leading figure of Qingyi (female role) acting, has recently passed away. Wang Yaoqing alone remains, like a surviving spiritual light of the Lu Temple. In the old days, his ingenious and unique creation of new vocal styles brought about a great change in the style of female roles. The Mei, Cheng, Xun, and Shang generations followed suit and further developed it. As times changed, it became a global craze. Those with a Zhou Yu-like appreciation immediately felt refreshed, and ancient beauties such as the weeping Qing in "Burying Flowers" and the Hongfu in "The Runaway Bride" have since become ubiquitous on singing and dancing stages.

In recent years, the Shanghai opera scene has mostly called upon consecutive stage plays. Although their novel costumes and magical stage settings are not favored by those who appreciate the nuances of music, their emphasis on showing off and creating novelty is enough to attract the attention of the contemporary public. These people have no choice but to do so for the sake of business, so it is not too critical.

However, there are still quite a few members of the community who are passionate about this art form and meticulously adhere to the models of the past. Perhaps this is an example of seeking what is lost in the countryside. Taking a corner of the city as an example, the number of amateur opera troupes is like bamboo shoots after a spring rain. The rising star, the Mingxing Opera Troupe, has been gaining increasing renown since its two rehearsals. It was previously reported that they were seeking sponsoring members, and in less than two months, they raised a huge sum of 6,000 gold. The community's expectations for the troupe and their strong interest in Peking Opera can be seen from this. It is also heard that the troupe's third rehearsal will be held soon, with completely new costumes recently purchased. This is another example of perseverance in the amateur community. We should look forward to witnessing the performances of famous operas and satisfying our eyes.

New Knowledge for the Family

— Tianshu Wosheng (Compiled)

Pure honey essence should only use refined glycerin (Glyceine) that has been distilled through bone charcoal to remove sacrificial substances such as sulfuric acid. It is best not to add any impurities. However, the common problem of manufacturers is always to cut corners to reduce costs, either by adding some water or mixing in some syrup. Its effect is also changed. Because the purpose of applying glycerin on the skin is to absorb moisture from the air to moisturize the skin. Now that water has been added to it, what will it absorb? Moreover, glycerin applied on the skin can remove the brown pigment in the skin caused by sunlight and make the skin white and tender, and prevent wrinkles. If syrup is used to replace it, what use is it? Therefore, people who are generally discerning must buy foreign goods to use. In fact, the pure honey essence of the Invincible brand is as good as foreign honey. Just try to compare it: (1) Turn the glass bottle sideways to see how fast the bubbles inside move. (2) Dip a piece of paper in it and burn it to see what happens. (3) Apply it to the palm of your hand to see if it is oily. These three methods are the simplest. If water has been added, the bubbles will move very quickly and disappear in the blink of an eye. If syrup is mixed in, it will turn into charcoal when burned. If syrup and water are applied to the palm of the hand, it will only be sticky and not oily. Applying powder will turn it into a pile that cannot be smeared evenly. That is a disfiguring product, not a beauty product. We should be aware of this. (Lord of Kan Yun Lou)

(Attached note) Invincible brand pure honey essence is available in all department stores. The label clearly states "Invincible Brand Pure Honey Essence." The large bottle (6 taels) is priced at 60 cents, the medium bottle (4 taels) is priced at 45 cents, and the small bottle (2 taels) is priced at 30 cents. There is also an 8-tael bottle of the highest-quality honey essence, priced at one yuan per bottle. For mail orders of half a dozen or more, no additional postage will be charged.

Travelogue of Southeast Asia (52)

— Linghua

On the morning of the 19th, I took a public bus to the zoo, which was founded by the monk Fakong of the Kek Lok Si Temple. The admission ticket was 40 cents, but I was given a free pass. Inside, there were African crowned cranes, guinea fowl, Indian Peng birds, and a Malayan earthworm that was two feet in diameter and one and a half feet wide, with long hair like clothes, which was quite a spectacle. The African ghost king monkey was given a banana, but it bared its teeth and snarled at people, both frightening and disgusting. The white-bearded monkey and the long-tailed monkey were very tame. Although they are all monkeys, their nature is not equally good or bad. The white-bearded monkey has a beard under its chin, and its tail is longer than its body. Its fur is five-colored. The white monkey and the five-colored monkey each cost over a thousand yuan, which is very expensive. They are not very big. They are all monkeys, but it is expensive. I do not understand such inequality. The Indian black lion monkey is quite elegant. There are also white-eyed and white-mouthed monkeys, with white circles around their eyes and mouths, like clowns in a play. All of them are tame. There are also yellow-eared and yellow-mouthed monkeys. There are over a hundred species of monkeys, with varying degrees of ferocity and tameness, differences in size, and variations in fur color. Some bare their teeth at each other when given food, some are greedy and dissatisfied, and some are content with little. I was moved by the differences in the nature of the monkey species and sighed at the extreme inequality in human nature, physiology, psychology, strength, weakness, good, evil, tameness, violence, male, and female. Is it not contrary to reality to treat people as uniformly equal? If monkeys cannot be equal, how can people be equal? I would like scholars of anthropology and sociology to answer this question. Chu Bawang was born with a stuttering voice, and Yan Ying was born less than seven feet tall. Emperor Wen of Han was kind and amiable, while Dou Yuejiao of Chu was born with the appearance of a bear and the voice of a jackal. How can those who are born bad and harm society be equal? Therefore, Confucius said, "Only the wise and the foolish do not change." I see the inequality among monkeys and sigh at the fact that the theory of human equality is not in line with reality. It is said that Rousseau advocated equality in the 18th century, while his friend Voltaire opposed it. Voltaire (1654-1778) Rousseau believed in popular revolution, while Voltaire ridiculed it, saying that if equality wins, freedom is lost. Voltaire and Rousseau were both key figures in promoting the French Revolution, but they differed fundamentally. The socialist Saint-Simon also opposed the idea of equality. Saint Simon. Even Marx, whom Russia believes in, did not believe in equality. Therefore, Lenin openly used an autocratic system of execution. A friend of the philosopher De Witts said that numbers cannot produce wisdom, and the masses are difficult to reason with. Socrates was killed in Athens because of the inequality of the parliament, and he was very saddened by human opinion. Jesus was crucified in Judea because it was decided by the Pharisees. Alas, I see the inequality in monkey society and am very saddened by the difficulty of aligning mankind. In the past, Ban Gu's Table of People divided people into nine grades, while Mr. Sun Yat-sen divided people into eight grades, with distinctions between the wise, talented, mediocre, and foolish, as well as the equality of flat heads and the equality of flat feet. Mr. Sun Yat-sen's lifelong revolutionary goal was to seek freedom and equality for mankind, and that was how he explained equality. Then, can people not deeply consider the meaning of equality and act blindly?

A pair of large white swans are extremely beautiful in the White Tao River. This is the bird praised in Kropotkin's theory of mutual aid, which has a highly moral group nature and can feed blind birds in its group. Confucius's Great Harmony first emphasized supporting the elderly, but now the elderly are despised. Are we really inferior to these swan birds?

Warmth in My Heart (279)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 14: Emerald Bamboo Sheds Tears, the Beauty's Heart is Broken; Red Lotus Loses Its Fragrance, a Maiden's Soul Departs

Cuiyun thought that her body had been sold. Unless she could pay back his money, but in the current situation, she could not pay back the money. What other options were there to consider? The only option was to endure. She hoped that Zhang Yiqing would treat her well and just get by, considering it a settled marriage. There was no talk of love, but compared to drifting outside, it was better. In these three months, it could be said that she had temporarily maintained the status quo. Because the other woman did not know about this small family. He went to Hankou by boat once a day, always for ten days. During these ten days, he spent all his time with Cuiyun. The woman at home was easily deceived because the elderly people at his old home would only get up when the sun was setting. However, calculating from a month, the other woman still got two-thirds of his time, while Cuiyun only got one-third. But this situation could not last forever, like lotus leaves wrapping water chestnuts, it could not be wrapped forever. As time went on, the secret would gradually leak out. One day, a steward on the Yangtze River steamer did not know their secret because that steward was recommended by this wife. Recently, he had been doing very well, just by bringing local products, he could earn dozens of dollars every month. So he specially bought some bronzeware in Hankou and some porcelain in Jiujiang to show his respect to the recommending benefactor. Without knowing it, he caused a problem. The steward's name was A Tu, born with some simple-mindedness. He knew that this wife got up late. In the evening, he presented what he had to offer like a Persian offering treasures. In addition to receiving his gifts, the wife casually asked what time your ship arrived today. A Tu said that the ship arrived the day before yesterday in the morning. Because there was something to do yesterday, I brought a little something today to visit the lady. The wife thought that the ship had already arrived the day before yesterday, so why didn't Yiqing come home yesterday? This matter was a little suspicious. She asked the comprador if he had seen him on the ship. A Tu said no, if the comprador was on the ship, we would definitely know. For example, when it was time to eat, we would eat with the second and third compradors. The wife said that he did not say that he took your ship to go and take your ship to come back? If A Tu was a little smarter, he would have known that they had other affairs. But this steward was a friend who [only bought bricks and not tiles] and insisted that the comprador was not on the ship. Not only was the comprador not on the downstream trip, but he was not on the upstream trip either. Fortunately, there was a maid beside the wife who prepared her smoking set, fearing that the master also had an affair with her, so she defended him, saying that maybe there was something going on in Hankou and the master stayed in Hankou to wait for the next shift. The wife said that even if he was waiting for the next shift downstream, he clearly said that he was taking this ship upstream.

Commercial News

Finance: The Gold Market Continues to Decline

Unpredictable fluctuations of ten taels. Yesterday, the 17th, the gold price continued to weaken. The market was sluggish and fluctuating, with variations of two or three taels being common. However, the entire market had a ten-tael swing, hovering around 40 taels from morning to night. The market was unpredictable and volatile. As for foreign exchange, it eased slightly, and banks made some purchases. Because the swap period had just passed, there were no clear figures. In the early market, Yongfeng and Yuanheng, etc., made some purchases, while Yuanmao, Yongyuan, and Shengjin, etc., had already sold. However, the demand for supply varied among the firms, and there was no sign of bold action. The early market was peaceful because silver bars remained unchanged. Later, rumors spread that there was internal strife in Japan and that opposition to the cabinet was very strong. As a result, people became fearful, and all parties were inclined to sell, suddenly breaking through the 40-tael mark and plummeting by about ten taels. The situation was turbulent, and the market seemed to be in a downward spiral. Furthermore, because buyers were diligent and the exchange rate turned flat, it was pulled up by three taels. Afterwards, the firms sold vigorously at first, but then chased to buy. However, because there was no market for bills of exchange on Wednesdays, and the gold price suddenly fell to 27 taels and 5 mace. Finally, it exceeded the 40-tael mark again. It was found that the low cost of this swap period was actually due to the abundance of cash. Fuchang used to hold a long position, but now it has intensified, turning more to short selling. It is estimated that the October period is still short more than 5,000 contracts. Before the swap date, they prepared to settle in cash because the spot goods collected in September could be sold off. Yesterday, some retail investors who were long also hurriedly dropped out, but the shorts refused to swap, so there was talk of a flat drop.

The market opened peacefully in the morning, then suddenly dropped sharply. The opening price for November was slightly down by 7 cents, totaling 547 taels. The silver price rose slightly by one-eighth, but without much impact. The gross price fell from 47.5 taels to 42.5 taels. The sellers were particularly bold, especially the large firms, who saw a rebound and first announced a price of 43.45 taels, but did not change the listing price. The internal market was still stable. HSBC and the Mai Bank bought British gold for December at 8 pence and for November at 7.9375 pence. Then, they increased the price by two taels to 44.67 taels. After 10 o'clock, the situation deteriorated further due to rumors that the Japanese cabinet might be unstable, causing extreme fear among the general public. Moreover, major firms competed to sell. Dadesheng and Yuancheng, etc., sold heavily, so the price plummeted. Shortly after, it broke through 40 taels and fell to only 38 taels at 11 o'clock. However, there was a fluctuation of one or two taels, and the exchange rate was also weak. Page 13

Local News

Shanghai City Fundraising for the 19th Year

Measures for Customs Treasury Bills

Borrowing Rent for Two Months

Divided into Two Instalments

Implemented on October 1st

The Shanghai Municipal Government, under orders to raise short-term Customs Treasury Bills for the 19th year, organized the Shanghai City Fundraising Committee for the 19th Year Customs Treasury Bills to carry out the fundraising. A meeting was held at the Municipal Government Staff Recreation Club on Weihaiwei Road. Attendees included Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Xu Jiyuan, Qin Runqing, Ye Huijun, Wang Yiting, Shen Lianfang, Wang Binyan, Zhang Xiaoliang, Xu Fu, Huang Jin, Shen Tianshen, Yu Hongjun, Yuan Liang, Tang Naikang, Pan Gongzhan, Shen Yi, Zhu Yan, Hu Hongji, Xu Yuanfang, Zhu Hao, and more than 30 others. Chairman Yu Hongjun and Recorder Wang Shaoqi reported that the central government's military victories at the front were expected to end soon, but military supplies and government expenses urgently needed replenishment. Therefore, 50 million yuan of short-term Customs Treasury Bills for the 19th year were issued. The Shanghai Municipal Government was ordered to raise 1 million yuan. As a central government agency, the Municipal Government had a duty to promote the treasury bills. After discussion at the municipal affairs meeting, a fundraising committee was organized, and the mayor appointed the attendees as members. As Chairman Jiang's telegrams had been repeatedly received, urging payment, there was no time to delay. Therefore, the attendees were asked to discuss fundraising measures together. Many of the attendees were local elders, closely linked to the Municipal Government. It was hoped that they would provide strong support to raise the required amount to meet urgent needs. Then, Tang Naikang reported on the process of receiving orders for fundraising. Subsequently, members such as Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Qin Runqing, Ye Huijun, and Shen Tianshen expressed their opinions. It was then decided to borrow rent in exchange for treasury bills. The detailed measures for borrowing rent would be formulated and implemented by the Municipal Government. The Municipal Government then presented the temporary municipal affairs meeting, which approved it and appointed Councilor Xu, Director Tang, Director Pan, Director Zhu, and Director Yuan to discuss the detailed measures for borrowing rent together. A number of proposed measures were then reported (1) The Municipal Government should widely announce the resolution of the Fundraising Committee. (2) The Finance Bureau should be ordered to handle the borrowing of rent and formulate various regulations and budgets. (3) The Public Security Bureau should be ordered to assist the Finance Bureau in borrowing rent. (4) The Public Security Bureau should announce a crackdown on rent arrears and earnestly implement it. All of the above items have been reviewed and approved by the Municipal Government, and orders have been issued to the Finance and Public Security Bureaus for compliance, along with an announcement and publication of the regulations, which are specially recorded as follows:

Announcement

Announcement regarding the fundraising for the 19th year short-term Customs Treasury Bills in this city. The matter has been submitted to the 164th Municipal Affairs Meeting of this government. It was resolved to organize a fundraising committee for the 19th year Customs Treasury Bills to raise the required amount on schedule. It was also resolved to borrow rent for two months in exchange for treasury bills and to formulate and implement 12 interim regulations. In addition to distribution, a public announcement is hereby made to all citizens, who should each act with a sense of public spirit and contribute to this endeavor. It should be known that the livelihood of the people and the national economy are closely related, and every citizen has a responsibility for the security situation. The issuance of treasury bills by the central government is originally intended to regulate surpluses and deficits. The guarantees are extremely secure, and the interest rates are also very favorable. The borrowing of rent in this city is also a balanced and responsible obligation. Moreover, the burden is not excessive. In this time of national crisis, the people of Shanghai should naturally not yield to others in generously contributing and always take the lead. Furthermore, this plan is being implemented in various provinces and cities, and Shanghai is widely expected to enthusiastically subscribe, so how can we lag behind others? It is hoped that the citizens will understand that the government is sincere and striving to meet the central government's expectations. It is the sincere hope of this government to commend the citizens and also to protect the legitimate interests of landlords to the greatest extent possible. Rights and obligations are inherently balanced, and public and private interests will naturally benefit both. Treasury bills are no different from savings, and purchasing them is not the same as reckless spending. However, the deadline for treasury bills is approaching, and the government's need for funds is urgent. It is hoped that subscriptions will be made quickly so that reports can be made in time. No delays or wait-and-see attitudes should be taken, as this would delay important needs. The matter is imperative, and there is no room for evasion. You are expected to comply. This is an announcement.

Regulations

Shanghai Municipal Government Regulations for Raising 19th Year Customs Duty Short-Term Treasury Bonds by Collecting Advance Rent:

Article 1: This city has been ordered to raise 1,000,000 yuan in 19th-year customs duty short-term treasury bonds. According to the resolution of the 19th-year customs duty treasury bond raising committee, this will be done by collecting advance rent in exchange for treasury bonds.

Article 2: All houses within the Shanghai city limits, except those belonging to government agencies or those falling under the circumstances listed in Article 5 of these regulations, shall be subject to the collection of two months' advance rent according to the provisions of these regulations.

Article 3: The collection period shall begin on October 1st of the 19th year and shall be collected in two installments within two months.

Article 4: Those with a monthly rent of less than three yuan shall be exempt from this advance collection.

Article 5: Vacant houses, charitable organizations, statutory bodies, and schools that conform to the provisions of Articles 5 and 6 of the city's regulations for collecting house tax and have been approved for exemption from house tax on record shall be exempt from this advance collection.

Article 6: This advance rent shall be collected by personnel dispatched by the four tax collection offices (East, South, West, and North) of the Municipal Bureau, who shall be temporarily issued badges for identification.

Article 7: The amount of rent to be advanced by each household shall be based on the rent amount listed on the most recent house tax receipt.

Article 8: This advance rent shall be collected from the tenants, who shall be given a receipt to be handed over to the landlords as full payment of the rent. The landlords shall not refuse to accept it.

Article 9: A receipt shall be issued for each household according to the house number. If there are several households at one house number, a single receipt shall be issued for all of them.

Article 10: After the formal treasury bonds are issued, the Municipal Finance Bureau shall issue a notice for the exchange of the receipts for 19th-year customs duty short-term treasury bonds at designated banks.

Article 11: If a collector is found to be overcharging or making excessive demands, the victim may report it to the responsible authority for strict punishment according to the law. Those who intentionally reduce or evade payment through bribery shall be punished equally.

Article 12: These regulations shall take effect from the date of their promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Sino-Japanese Labor Dispute Resolved Yesterday

Nine Resolution Measures Signed

Resumption of Work on the 22nd

The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau mediated the strike dispute at the Pudong Sino-Japanese Cotton Mill. As of September 16th, the two sides had reached a deadlock at the mediation table due to a dispute over the bonus issue in the second clause. At that time, the mediation chairman, Guo Yongxi, had also instructed both parties to apply for arbitration according to the law. However, yesterday, the labor and management of the factory voluntarily negotiated a settlement and jointly signed nine settlement measures at the Social Affairs Bureau, thus resolving the dispute. The details are as follows:

The Course of Events: The Social Affairs Bureau initially worked with the Municipal Civil Training Association to send personnel to mediate repeatedly without success. The Municipal Government then ordered another mediation meeting to be convened according to law. Therefore, a mediation was started on September 12th, and continued on the 15th and 16th for a total of two mediations, but the sides were still not close to agreement.

The Process of Settlement: On the mediation table, the Social Affairs Bureau mediation chairman, Guo Yongxi, inquired about the reasons for the reconciliation of labor and management at the factory.

(1) The labor representatives replied that after yesterday's mediation broke down, they returned to convene various representatives for discussion and unanimously believed that at a time of emergency in the front-line military situation, the rear's security was extremely important. If the work stoppage was prolonged, it would inevitably disrupt social order, and the workers' livelihoods would be difficult after two months of striking, and they would be unable to maintain themselves if work was not resumed. However, the condition for resuming work was to exchange the dismissal of four people by the factory: Fei Wanqing, Ding Zhuo, Ni Chenglu, and Zhang Hanhui. Therefore, they are now requesting a settlement and signing. If the factory continues to keep these four people working at the factory, there will inevitably be many disputes in the future, so their dismissal is absolutely necessary.

(2) The management representatives replied that there was no permission to dismiss the four people during yesterday's discussion. However, before the investigation is completed, the four are not allowed to enter the factory to work. The chairman said that since the two sides voluntarily settled, the date of resumption of work should first be determined. The labor representatives stated: (A) The daily worker who repairs the motors can enter the factory on Friday. (B) Due to time constraints, all workers are allowed to resume work on Monday of next week (the 22nd). However, there are two conditions to be included in the contract after this resumption of work: (1) The wages deducted for errors by workers in each workshop shall not exceed five points. (2) Workers shall not be dismissed without reason after resumption of work. After the chairman consulted the management's opinions and repeatedly persuaded them, they finally yielded and signed the settlement agreement.

The Provisions of the Settlement: The provisions of the settlement measures are as follows:

(1) The workers of the Ri-Hua Cotton Mill asked the factory to increase the rice subsidy, which will not be discussed for the time being. Starting from September, the factory will pay each person a monthly bonus of eight dimes until the end of October (according to the summer bonus method).

(2) The factory must award one day's wages to each worker who works a full half month. Those who work a full week of day work and a week of night work within half a month will be awarded two days' wages. The original two cents of silver dollars for each night worker's dinner subsidy is canceled. The factory agrees to give one day of bonus pay for those who have not worked for two full weeks before this strike.

(3) Wages must not be delayed if the work is not sufficient.

(4) The Social Affairs Bureau will send personnel to investigate and verify the case of the factory dismissing Yu Qixiang and other seven people for review and handling.

(5) Fei Wanqing and other four persons agitator of the labor unrest case are not allowed to enter the factory to work before the investigation is clarified.

(6) Wages will be paid for four days during the strike period (not paid to those who do not report for work within ten days after resumption of work).

(7) All workers must resume work at 9:00 AM on the 22nd of this month. The repairers and the daily workers of the motor manager are allowed to go to work first at 2:00 PM on the 18th.

(8) The wages deducted for errors by workers in each workshop shall not exceed five points.

(9) Workers shall not be dismissed without reason after resumption of work.

Attending personnel: Chairman Guo Yongxi (seal), Municipal Party Committee Mao Yun (seal), Public Security Bureau Gong Yushuo (seal), Labor representatives Yu Qixiang (seal), Chen Xiaofang (signature), Hu Shoulin (signature), Gu Lanru (signature), Pu Liang (signature), Wang Zhaozhi (signature), Management representatives Tsuji Keisho (seal), Nishimura Yoshizo (seal), Recorder Wang Zhixin, September 17, 19th Year of the Republic of China.

Japanese Trade Report with China

Recent Situation and Expansion

Japan attaches the utmost importance to foreign trade, and it is making every effort to promote Japanese goods in the Chinese market, especially in Shanghai. The business of importing and exporting in Shanghai in August was affected by the current situation, and most of them showed a declining trend. However, the situation in Sino-Japanese trade within this month was not bad. The Japanese authorities in this port compiled and investigated the Sino-Japanese trade in August and obtained the following overview:

Import and Export Volume: The total value of Japanese goods imported into Shanghai in August was 47 million yuan, while the value of exports from this port to Japan was 37 million yuan. Compared with the same period last year, the import was 53.5 million yuan and the export was 38.7 million yuan. In contrast, this year's Japanese goods arriving in Shanghai are not as good as last year.

Sugar Sales: Japanese sugar sales in our country are very large. Before the Mid-Autumn Festival, when mooncakes are put on the market, the amount of Japanese sugar transported to our country is always greater than usual. Japanese sugar merchants expect to sell one million bags before the Mid-Autumn Festival, of which 300,000 bags will be sold in the Yangtze River area, 300,000 bags in the French Concession, 200,000 bags in the North and South Oceans, and 200,000 bags in other ports. Currently, there are 300,000 bags of Japanese sugar stored in Shanghai, so recent Japanese sugar imports are being rushed.

Ship Berthing: In August, the shipping industry was the most sluggish. The reason was that transportation in various places was affected by the current situation, and the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River were harassed by Communist Party disturbances. Therefore, there were 22,000 tons of ships berthed at this port, totaling 3,000 to 5,000 tons of ships that suspended operations in the Huangpu River.

Cotton Textile Industry: The factories in Shanghai have recently been affected by strikes for more than 45 days, so their business has suffered considerable losses, especially the textile industry.

Meeting and Expansion: The Japanese authorities in Shanghai, in order to discuss the development of trade with China, gathered important Japanese merchants last Saturday to hold a meeting to discuss how to proceed. The details of the discussion are being kept secret and will not be announced.

After starting service in July, it only ran once due to improvements in the machinery and boilers, and then underwent major repairs. This is the first Yangtze River diesel fast ship, and Jardine Matheson is also rushing to build the new "Baohe" ship in order to compete, and plans to start sailing in early October, also on the Shanghai-Yichang route.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Request to Re-Examine Trade Regulations

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce presented a document to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday regarding the issue of trade compliance with industry regulations, stating:

Regarding the presentation, on the 16th of this month, Instruction No. 1820 from your Bureau was received, opening the case. Instruction No. 5624 from the Municipal Government was received, and it contains Instruction No. 3225 from the Executive Yuan:

Regarding the issue of acting on the order: The Chairman issued document No. 4552 from the Civil Service Office of the National Government, stating that the trade regulations presented by the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce after the resolution of the members' representative assembly and approved for registration by the trade association should be regarded as special regulations for the industry issued by the government. All trades not entering the association should also comply, which is essential to remedy the dissolution of the national system. The case was transferred to the Executive Yuan for review. In response, a copy of the original document was enclosed for reference and handling. The Municipal Government's document No. 235 was copied and forwarded, requesting a review. The case was transferred to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for review. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce replied that trade regulations are not laws and cannot be enforced, and the trade regulations set by various industries often contain monopolistic characteristics or violate good customs. The supervisory authority is not aware of the industry's situation, and even if it is filed, it is still difficult to ensure that there will be no abuses. Such bad regulations, in legal terms, are difficult to protect even if taken to court. Why should trades be forced to comply with them? Therefore, regardless of the content of the regulations, all regulations approved by the government, whether entered or not, must be complied with, which not only does not help but also causes disputes. The statement in the presentation that trades not entering the association should also comply with the regulations is not appropriate. The review and reply from the Ministry are acceptable. In addition to instructing and recording the case and replying to the Civil Service Office for submission, the Municipal Government should be instructed to investigate and handle the case.

In this case, the Bureau previously forwarded the presentation to the Municipal Government after review and informed it. Before receiving the order, the association was ordered to investigate and handle the case and forward the information for notice. Underneath, it says that the official authority’s responsibility is to handle industrial and commercial affairs within the area under its jurisdiction. If the regulations requested for registration by various industries have monopolistic implications or violate good customs, it is difficult to approve them easily. All cases of rejection can be investigated. The order of the department states that even if it has been filed, it is still difficult to ensure that there will be no abuses. The official management seems unlikely to be so careless. It also states that this type of bad industry regulations is difficult to protect even if filed in court. If such a statement is established, even if trades entering the association file lawsuits in order to protect their interests, they will not be guaranteed. The association has stated that all industry regulations are not enough to bind those who are not members of the association and even the members of the association, the association has no binding force, not to mention the welfare and benefits of the trade. The country's permission to establish trade associations is clearly recognized as being for the maintenance of public interest and to correct business abuses. If the regulations approved for registration by various trade associations are denounced as "often containing monopolistic characteristics and violating good customs", then the establishment of trade associations is tantamount to creating a monopolistic organization for the trade. If this is true, wouldn't merchants file lawsuits and wouldn't the authorities dissolve these trade associations? The focus of the departmental order is that most of the industry regulations do not conform to good customs and that the authorities have not been able to review them in detail, so even if they are filed, it is difficult to ensure that there are no abuses. This level should be explained by the authorities in detail without redundant statements from the association. However, since the departmental order states that the supervisory authority should still carefully review the industry regulations with reference to good commercial practices in order to reduce disputes, and that if the content of the regulations does not violate good commercial customs, after careful review and approval by the government, it is tantamount to a recognized business practice of the industry. If the scope of travel is limited to member of the association, those who are not members of the association will take advantage of personal interests, and the members of the association will withdraw one after another, the association will collapse like a tile and will only exist in form. It is not an empty talk. The operating practices of an industry that do not conflict with commercial laws and regulations have the effect of supplementing the legal effectiveness of the practice. The agreed filing of industry regulations is actually the written commercial customs. It cannot be said that it has no compulsory effect in terms of the common example of supplementing laws and regulations with customs, and the order for non-member trades to comply is indeed necessary according to the facts and is not without a basis in law. Therefore, it is appropriate to submit a document to the Bureau for your review and approval of whether to continue to submit a request to the Municipal Government, or to the Ministry or the Executive Yuan, to ask them to re-examine the matter. The Bureau's decision will be awaited with anticipation.

Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau

Explanation of Union Membership Qualifications

Previously, the Chinese and Foreign Cotton Industry Workers' Union had presented a request to the Municipal Council due to ambiguities in the Trade Union Law regarding the qualifications for union membership. The Municipal Council then forwarded the request for interpretation. The Bureau's instruction, which had been received, stated (above omitted). Now, Municipal Government Instruction No. 5655 states: "Upon reviewing the aforementioned request from the Chinese and Foreign Cotton Industry Workers' Union for an interpretation of the qualifications for union membership as stipulated in the Trade Union Law, this request was forwarded and presented for compliance. It has been instructed by the Executive Yuan that the Bureau is to be informed. Executive Yuan Instruction No. 3209 states: 'The Ministry has submitted a response stating that regarding the original request: (1) If a worker, having obtained membership qualifications according to Article 1 or 2 of the Trade Union Law, is subsequently appointed as an employer or their agent in the same occupation or industry, does their membership still exist? According to the proviso of Article 2 of the Trade Union Law, employers or their agents are not included. Therefore, employers or their agents are not qualified to join a union as members. Consequently, when a member is appointed as an employer or their agent, their membership should cease to exist. (2) If a union member loses their membership due to being appointed as an employer or agent in a different occupation or industry, and later returns to being a worker, is their membership automatically restored, or must they apply for union membership again? Obtaining union membership requires applying for membership, and the continuation of membership should follow the same procedure to be compliant. Therefore, if a member loses their membership due to being appointed as an employer or their agent in the same occupation or industry, they must reapply for union membership upon returning to work as a worker to regain their membership. (3) If a worker possesses the qualifications in Article 1, Sections 1 and 2, of the Trade Union Law and joins a union in a different occupation or industry, can they then join a union in the same occupation or industry as a member? According to Article 19 of the Trade Union Law, a worker may only join a union in the same industry or occupation. The fundamental principle of this law is that one worker can only join one union. A member who has already joined a union in a different occupation or industry cannot join another union until they withdraw from the first union. (4) If a worker in location A requests a transfer of membership to a union in the same occupation or industry in location B due to a change in work location, can the union in location B charge a membership fee and require them to fill out a union application form, or can the union in location A transfer their membership fee and application form to the union in location B? Although the unions in location A and location B belong to the same industry or occupation, their organizations are not connected and remain separate entities. Therefore, if a member of the union in location A requests to join the union in location B due to a change in work location, it should not be regarded as a transfer of membership, and the membership continuation procedure should be followed accordingly.' Upon receiving and reviewing the Ministry's response, it is deemed appropriate. In addition to instructions, the Municipal Government is hereby ordered to investigate and handle the matter accordingly." Following this order, the Bureau is hereby ordered to comply and instruct compliance. Following this order, the Union is hereby ordered to comply.

Petitions from Various Trade Unions

Abolish Old Practices of Dismissal

Various trade unions in the city, because the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau had announced that the dismissal of employees would temporarily follow the old practices of various industries, believing this hindered the original labor-capital contracts and caused many labor-capital disputes, jointly petitioned the Municipal Training Council to request the Municipal Government to order the Social Affairs Bureau to revoke Announcement No. 146. The petition stated: "[Petition for the revocation of Social Affairs Bureau Announcement No. 146 by order of the Municipal Government to uphold the labor movement. We, the unions, believe that the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's Announcement No. 146 of August 8, which allows the temporary use of old industry practices for the hiring and firing of employees, and the news reported in various local newspapers on August 26 regarding the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's investigation into industry dismissal practices, have caused widespread anxiety. It is clear that various industries in this city have established legal group organizations, and most have signed labor-capital contracts with articles stipulating dismissal methods. Why should there be any further changes or a need to continue using old, outdated practices? This is why we are requesting the revocation of Social Affairs Bureau Announcement No. 146. Firstly, the various trade unions in this city have been legally organized, and the existing labor-capital contracts they have concluded should be jointly observed by both labor and capital. In the past, the Social Affairs Bureau has issued clear statements during holidays and festivals, stating that employers in various industries must not use old practices to dismiss employees without reason. This is why we are requesting the revocation of Social Affairs Bureau Announcement No. 146. Secondly, it has been possible to maintain peace and stability when the industries have stipulated that employees cannot be dismissed without reason. If the old dismissal practices of the three sections are allowed to be used, there will be unlimited hiring and firing of employees, and the rights of the original contract will inevitably be stripped away. The number of unemployed workers will increase in our backward industrial and commercial nation, and social order may be disrupted. This is why we are requesting the revocation of Social Affairs Bureau Announcement No. 146. Thirdly, in the past, labor-capital disputes have arisen because workers were dismissed without reason, leading to the escalation of labor unrest that was difficult to resolve. The disputes were only resolved after party and government agencies repeatedly convened meetings to mediate and sign contracts. Now, the Social Affairs Bureau has clearly announced that employers can use the old dismissal practices of the three sections, which will only lead to more disputes and be of no benefit to employers, causing social unrest. This is why we are requesting the revocation of Social Affairs Bureau Announcement No. 146. Fourthly, in summary, Announcement No. 146 of the Social Affairs Bureau has a significant impact on the future of the labor movement and social order. We are compelled to express our concerns and request that your Council swiftly forward this petition to the Municipal Government, ordering the Social Affairs Bureau to revoke the aforementioned announcement immediately. The labor movement will be fortunate, and the party and nation will be fortunate. Respectfully submitted (below omitted).]"

Silk Industry Pre-Orders Japanese Silkworm Eggs

Ordering 80,000 Silkworm Egg Cards

To Prevent a Cocoon Shortage Next Year

The production of summer and autumn cocoons in this city and other areas has not been very smooth, and the quality is relatively poor, which has caused considerable concern among silk factories. Previously, Japanese cocoons were purchased and imported as a temporary remedy. However, due to opposition from various parties, this could not be continued. Yesterday, it was learned that the silk industry is planning to contact Japan to pre-order silkworm eggs in order to prevent a cocoon shortage next year and improve the quality. Contact has already been made, and it is planned to ship as many as 800 cards of silkworm eggs to China next spring. The Japanese government, in order to encourage the export of silkworm eggs to China, plans to issue certificates of conformity to prove their quality.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Request for Thorough Investigation of Tax Card Detention of Yarn

The Municipal Council sent a letter to the Special Commissioner of Finance for Jiangsu Province, stating: "On the 15th of this month, according to a letter from the Local River Steamer Association of this city, a member of our association, Xie Xing Steamer Bureau, reported that on September 7, their steamer Xie Feng towed a cargo ship to Changshu. As usual, they declared and submitted their tax tickets at the tax card checkpoint in Taipu Temple. However, the yarn tax inspectors claimed that the yarn tax was incorrect. The ship's escort declared that the ten pieces of yarn loaded from the Huacheng Cloth Factory in Jiangyin today had the same tax tickets and were not incorrect. They requested that the inspectors check and verify the tickets to avoid delay and prevent the ship from falling behind schedule. However, the inspectors were stern and insisted that there must be an inconsistency and that five pieces of yarn must be deposited before the ship could be released. Seeing the situation was unfavorable, the ship's escort had no choice but to instruct the crew to delay departure and report back to the bureau. After learning about the situation, the bureau immediately dispatched six colleagues to Zhou Temple to meet with Mr. Xu and Mr. Shen of the yarn tax inspection office, requesting that they re-verify the tickets and confirm that there were no inconsistencies. They were immediately released, but this incident caused a delay of more than twelve hours. The steamer waited with its fires burning, consuming a large amount of coal, and the arrival was inevitably delayed. Passengers and cargo owners complained, resulting in a loss of credit and money for no reason. The situation is truly unbearable. Our bureau has never engaged in the practice of underreporting taxes. Now, the inspectors intentionally created difficulties, neither checking the packages nor making a prompt decision. If this continues, the consequences will be dire. We have no choice but to submit a letter detailing the events of that day, requesting that the Council forward it to the Jiangsu Provincial Special Tax Bureau for a strict prohibition against future detentions of ships under false pretenses, and to impose appropriate punishment on the inspectors in order to maintain navigation and facilitate transportation." Upon receiving the letter, the Council believes that the ten pieces of cotton yarn were not a large quantity and could have been easily checked. However, the inspectors ignored the facts and made false accusations, creating difficulties intentionally. It is feared that the inspectors would not be able to justify their actions. Therefore, we are submitting this letter to request that the Council forward it to the Jiangsu Provincial Special Tax Bureau for a thorough investigation and appropriate punishment to maintain navigation and deter improper practices. Upon review, the Tax Bureau should handle its affairs fairly, emphasizing both taxation and consideration for merchants. The Xie Feng Steamer Bureau loaded ten pieces of cotton yarn and passed through the Zhou Taipu Temple. If the tax card checkpoint suspected that the tax tickets were incorrect, it was within their authority to check the items. Since the number of items was small, it would have been easy to verify the tickets without hindering taxation or navigation. This would have been the proper way to handle the situation. However, the tax card checkpoint did not immediately verify the tickets but insisted on depositing the yarn as collateral, knowing that the steamer bureau would be held responsible by the customers for delivering fewer pieces of yarn. This unnecessary procedure was intentionally used to cause trouble for Xie Feng. By the time the bureau sent personnel to plead for a re-verification and the tickets were confirmed to be correct, the ship's departure had been delayed by more than twelve hours. The responsibility for the wasted coal and the losses incurred by cargo owners and passengers due to the delayed arrival should be borne by whom? If the blame lies with the steamer bureau, then Xie Feng Steamer had neither over-declared nor underreported the yarn and had repeatedly requested a verification of the yarn. The tax card point had no cause to make a false accusation and should follow the order to examine the cargo, so there was no reason to delay the shipping by 12 hours. Therefore, in this case, the fault lies with the tax card. Given the aforementioned situation, we are requesting that your office inform the Special Tax Bureau to investigate the personnel responsible for the delay and punish them accordingly to serve as a warning and prevent future occurrences. This will truly uphold public interests. Addressed to the Branch Office of the Special Commissioner of Finance for Jiangsu Province, Ministry of Finance.

Request for Relief for Victims of the Shaanxi-Sichuan Disaster

Report from the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee yesterday received a disaster relief letter from the Pucheng, Shaanxi branch of the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee, which is recorded below: "We are deeply grateful for your previous appeals, which have greatly benefited us. Unfortunately, the disaster situation in our Pucheng is compounded. Since the hailstorm in 1927, the land has been barren for more than three years, and no crops have been harvested. This year, there was still hope for an autumn harvest, but locusts have successively caused disasters, stripping and devouring all the autumn seedlings. The disaster is even more severe than before. If it were not for the relief efforts of various philanthropists, the ordinary victims would have no means of survival. Among the most tragic are the orphans and vulnerable women. Since the disaster, the strong have fled to all directions, and the old and weak have fallen into ditches. Those who remain are homeless children wandering about. The sound of their wailing is unbearable to hear, and their miserable state is unbearable to witness. Now that autumn is approaching and the weather is getting colder, if we do not set up a method to help them soon, they will inevitably die of cold and hunger. Our Association cannot bear to stand idly by, so we are planning to set up an orphanage and educational institution so that homeless children can enjoy both education and care. On the one hand, we will cultivate useful talents for the country, and on the other hand, we will live up to the enthusiasm of the various philanthropists who have provided relief. We know that the gentlemen of the sea are happy to do good deeds and will surely provide their support." The Association also received letters from Mr. Lin Kanghou, Mr. Su Minsheng, and Mr. Zhang Yuquan reporting on the Chongqing disaster as follows: "We have just received a telegram from the Chongqing General Chamber of Commerce in Sichuan, stating that a huge disaster has occurred, resulting in a great calamity. On the day in question, a fire broke out at Chuqimen in Chongqing due to negligence. The strong winds caused the fire to spread into the city, branching out and spreading north to Sanpai坊, west to Daliangzi, south to Jinzimen, and down to Taipingmen, turning everything into scorched earth. The suburbs are densely populated by the poor, and the city is a gathering place for commercial warehouses and merchants. The fire was finally extinguished at 10 p.m., covering an area of several miles and affecting more than 10,000 households. The victims were burned and scarred, and their cries shook the sky, creating an unprecedentedly tragic scene. We witnessed the tragedy and were heartbroken. In addition to supervising the various gangs of water dragons to put out the fire at the time, we inspected the rubble afterwards and saw endless piles of rubble and victims eating in the open air and waiting to be fed. We are now preparing emergency relief to provide temporary assistance, but the disaster area is too large and the need for relief is immense. Chongqing has suffered from years of military affairs and commercial difficulties, coupled with this year's severe drought. Just as it was beginning to recover, it suffered a major disaster. We can only send a telegram appealing to all parties, institutions, legal entities, merchants, philanthropists, and charitable people in all regions to have compassion for the severity of the disaster and to provide generous relief, so that not only will the tens of thousands of victims receive kindness, but the entire Chongqing people will be deeply grateful." Upon receiving this telegram, it was determined that the disaster in Chongqing was extremely severe, affecting tens of thousands of victims. Living in the open air during these autumn nights with autumn winds and rain is truly pitiful. Moreover, winter is approaching, and without food, how will they survive the year? Therefore, we are forwarding the telegram on their behalf, earnestly requesting that you quickly take steps to provide relief.

Red Cross Personal Constitution Committee

Continues Meeting

The Committee to Amend the Constitution of the Chinese Red Cross Society continued its meeting on the afternoon of September 16. The committee members present were Li Zhenbang, Wen Lanting, Ye Nansheng, Wang Peiyuan, Jiang Daqiu, Wang Wanlai, Liu Hongsheng, Xu Xichun, Xue Shaoting, Hong Yanbin, and others. Chairman Wen Lanting and Secretary Wei Ruifeng performed the formalities. The minutes of the previous meeting were read, and there were no objections. The Chairman signed the minutes. (1) The Chairman reported that today the regulations of the Executive Committee and the detailed rules of the branches of the Executive Committee would be read for the first time. Now, the regulations of the Executive Committee will be read first. (1) The Chairman said that the name of the Executive Committee should be changed to the Regulations of the Executive Committee of the Red Cross Society of the Republic of China. In addition, Article 16 should be changed to: "In order to handle the affairs of the Association, the Association shall establish six branches: Document, Economic, Disaster Relief, Medical, Youth, and Propaganda. Each branch shall have a director elected by the members of the Executive Committee, who shall handle all affairs of the Association. The detailed rules and regulations of the branches shall be stipulated separately, and a director may be hired to manage daily affairs under the supervision of the Executive Committee." (1) The Chairman reported that the regulations of the Executive Committee, except for the name and Article 16, should be passed. The first reading is now complete and the first reading of the detailed rules of the branches of the Executive Committee should continue. (1) Li Zhenbang said that the word "Economic" in Article 4, Paragraph 4, should be changed to "Assets." (1) Wang Peiyuan said that the word "Disaster" in Article 5, Paragraph 2, should be changed to "Disaster Situation." In addition, the responsibilities of the Youth Branch in Article 7 should be increased or decreased and submitted for discussion at the next meeting. In addition, a seventh item should be added to Article 6, which reads: "Establish a design for volunteer medical officers and nurses in accordance with the Constitution of the General Association." (1) The Chairman said that Item 5 of Article 8 should be changed to: "Send personnel to attend commemorative meetings held by various agencies at the location of the Association." Article 9 should be changed to: "Each branch shall have a director elected by the members of the Executive Committee." Article 10 should be changed to: "Each branch shall divide into sections to handle affairs according to the complexity of the work and shall establish a director, officer, recorder, or clerk as appropriate, who shall be nominated by the director of each branch and approved by the Executive Committee and appointed and dismissed by the Chairman." (1) The Chairman reported that the first readings of the regulations of the Executive Committee and the detailed rules of the branches were complete. The meeting will continue tomorrow for the second reading. The meeting adjourned at 5 p.m.

Customs Retroactively Issues Withheld Wages

The Jianghai Customs of this city, starting from January 1 of this year, increased the salaries of all its officers and clerks by 25% of their original salaries. However, no order was officially announced in advance. When the salaries were paid at the end of the month, all officers and clerks received an additional 12.5 cents per yuan. Therefore, everyone was happy to receive an additional 12.5 cents per yuan. However, 1.25 cents per yuan had already been deducted for eight or nine months. After this was discovered by a superior, a letter was sent to the heads of each branch stating that starting from June 1, the additional salary of 25 cents per yuan would continue to be paid, and the deducted amount of 1.25 cents per yuan for four months would be issued together with the salary at the end of September.

Local News Two

Botched Kidnapping, Three Die Tragically

Bandits Kill Chauffeur

Police Shoot Dead One Bandit

Infant Dies Tragically

Another Kidnapper Captured Alive

At around 10 a.m. yesterday, a kidnapping occurred suddenly at Rue du Père Robert in the French Concession. The bandits first robbed the hand pistol worn by a Chinese constable on duty at No. 186 on that road and then forced their way onto the victim's car, holding guns to watch over them. The bandits then expelled the chauffeur from the car. With a bandit at the wheel, attempting to start the car, the engine would not turn over as the driver had cut it off. This angered the bandits, and one fired three shots in succession, hitting the driver in the right chest, right rib and left leg. He fell instantly to the ground, dead with a pool of blood. The bandits abandoned the victim and scattered south in flight. At that moment, Detective Gao Xinfa, No. 50 of the French Concession Police, was patrolling nearby. On hearing the alarm he bravely rushed forward, catching one bandit and bringing him to the police station. Simultaneously, Chinese constable No. 98, hearing the alarm, rushed up to pursue a fleeing bandit, who was running south and firing back at the arresting officer. The Chinese constable returned fire, pursuing the robber as far as Dapu Bridge in the Chinese Settlement. There, with the help of police from the local area, they surrounded the bandit, who then bolted into a grass shack at No. 75 on the street and fired outwards, resisting arrest. By this time, the Lokawei Police Station had received a telephone call from patrolman No. 186, and Chief Beaulac, Detective Inspector Jin Jiu, Lee Chung, Detective Lee Yaolong, and detectives Guan Jinsheng, Guo Bingquan and others sped to the location and surrounded the building. The bandit was shot dead inside the shack. When the bandit ran into the shack he saw a baby and because it cried out loud he shot and killed it. The police then had the body of the dead chauffeur taken to the Tung Jen Fu Yuan Tang Funeral Parlor for an autopsy. According to Zhao Xiangbao, from Shaoxing, the captured bandit, the bandit killed in the Chinese area was named Yang Cai. He unhesitatingly confessed to conspiring and organising the kidnapping. District Chief Wang of the Second District then ordered the summoning of the local police chief and asked the court, along with the family of Wang Lianfu, the owner of No. 75, to examine the body of the two-year-old baby Xiao Sanzi.
