Yesterday's Execution of Pan Zhi

Criminal Convicted of Murdering an Englishman

Corpse Claimed After Post-Mortem Examination Today

Pan Zhi, a Cantonese man, was employed as an assistant to Mr. Greattree, an Englishman and customs official serving as a chief clerk. Seeing Mr. Greattree's luxurious lifestyle, Pan Zhi conceived a malicious plan to rob and murder him. On July 19th, at 1:00 AM, he took advantage of Mr. Greattree's deep sleep in his bedroom on the third floor of 859 North Szechuan Road. He broke into the room wielding a kitchen knife, killing his employer on the spot. He was immediately apprehended and sentenced to death by the Shanghai Special District Court. The sentence was submitted to and approved by the provincial government for execution by hanging. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Judge Cheng Shangfeng of the Special District Court ordered that the prisoner Pan be brought forth for identification. After confirming his identity, he instructed the concession police to escort the prisoner to the District Court for execution. The District Court appointed Prosecutor Yang Qi as the execution supervisor. Mr. Yang, along with Secretary Li Dingpan and Examiner Tong Zhiming, and ordered Police Chief Yang Deshan, Police Officer Chen Xihui, and selected executioners Gu Hanqing, Xue Bingzhang, Zhu WanYuan, and assistant Hu Xianglin, rushed to the Caohejing Second Prison execution ground. The prosecutor, together with Warden Dong, ascended to their official positions. The prisoner was brought forth and stated that he was 30 years old, from Xinhui, Guangdong, and had no fixed address in Shanghai. When asked if he had any last words for his family, he replied that a dying man had no need to trouble himself. The prosecutor immediately ordered the execution. Under the direction of Police Chief Yang, the executioners bound the prisoner as prescribed to a wooden stake, wrapped a rope around his neck, and slowly tightened it. The process lasted an hour. After the examiner confirmed the death, the secretary affixed a seal to the execution rope, to be examined again today before the body is claimed.

Huge Amount of Counterfeit Twenty-Cent Coins

Two Thousand Coins, a Considerable Number

Mixed into Circulation, Causing Significant Harm

Hongda Money Shop Arrests Three People

Hongda Fuji Small Money Shop, located at 208 Shandong Road, specialized in privately selling counterfeit twenty-cent and ten-cent coins. They sold them at a price of two silver dollars for fifteen counterfeit twenty-cent coins. Small cigarette and paper shops, solely for their own private gain, would purchase these counterfeit twenty-cent coins and mix them with genuine ones, passing them off. As a result, the number of counterfeit twenty-cent coins circulating in the market has been increasing daily, disrupting the financial system and causing significant harm. The most affected were various peddlers, who, after a day of hard work, if they unknowingly received one or two counterfeit coins, would see their day's earnings vanish. The General Inspectorate of the General Police Station had heard rumors of this and dispatched Detective Feng Shuofu to investigate. Only recently did they discover that the small money shop was the source of the counterfeit coins. They sent Chen Jixiang to purchase fifteen counterfeit coins, obtaining evidence. On the morning of the 10th, Chief Detective Lu Liankui, along with Detectives Pang Ruiqing, Feng Zhiming, and Officer Wu Hanzhang, rushed to Hongda Money Shop. A search revealed two thousand counterfeit twenty-cent coins and one hundred and forty-two counterfeit ten-cent coins, a considerable amount. The accountant, Shen Jinliang from Wuxi, and associates Dai Weixin from Zhenjiang and Wu Wuchang (also known as Wu Fuqi) from Yangzhou, were arrested. The owner of the shop was not found. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Shanghai Special District Court, where Judge Zhou Ting questioned them. The police's lawyer, Ru Baoyi, explained the police's investigation into the matter and requested a thorough interrogation. Shen and the other two claimed that the ten-cent coins were received as payments and that their silver content was slightly inferior, so they planned to send them to a silver smelter to be melted down. They hired lawyer Wang Fuchang to defend them. The court ordered the defendants to be held and investigated for seven days before further questioning.

Paper Pistols

Indistinguishable from Real Ones in the Dark

Used to Scare and Extort Rickshaw Pullers

Cai and Zhu Arrested Together

Cai Youlin and Zhu Jinde, both from Jiangbei, hired a rickshaw driven by Chen Chishi of the Huguangxing rickshaw company at around 1:00 AM yesterday in front of the Wing On Company on Nanjing Road, saying they were going to Yuezhou Road. As they passed Peng Road and Kunshan Garden, Officers No. 691 (Chinese) and No. 375 (Western) of the Hongkou Police Station were patrolling the area. Seeing Cai and Zhu traveling late at night and acting suspiciously, they ordered the rickshaw to stop for inspection. Cai suddenly threw something away and fled. The officers first apprehended Zhu and then chased and caught the fleeing Cai. They picked up the object Cai had discarded and saw that it was a pistol made of stiff cardboard. The cardboard was painted black, and when held in the hand in the dark, it was indistinguishable from a real pistol. They then searched Zhu and found another paper pistol hidden on his person. They immediately took them to the police station. At 9:00 AM, they were sent to the Shanghai Special District Court, and the two rickshaw pullers, Chen and Hu, were summoned to court to testify. Judge Feng questioned them about the purpose of carrying the objects. Cai confessed that due to prolonged unemployment and financial difficulties, he specially made the paper pistols and hid them on his person to scare and extort money from fellow rickshaw pullers from the same hometown. Last night, he and Zhu first hired two rickshaws and went to secluded places like Zhujiamuqiao, where they used the fake pistols to extort sixteen small silver coins and fourteen copper coins, which they split with Zhu. They then hired Chen's rickshaw and were about to use the same trick. He said the fake pistol was made by Zhu. Zhu admitted to making the fake pistol from cardboard and did not deny it. However, he claimed this was the first time they had used this method of extortion. It is deplorable that in these times, human hearts are not what they used to be and there are endless scams. The judge, fearing that Cai and Zhu might have committed other crimes, ordered them to be detained for further investigation.

Flower Gambling is Deeply Harmful

Addiction to Flower Gambling Leads to Economic Hardship

Unmarried Couple Dies Together

Guo Changqing (28 years old) from Shaoxing and his fiancée, Ms. Li (24 years old), were addicted to flower gambling. Recently, due to economic hardship, both had suicidal thoughts. At 8:00 PM, they checked into a room at the Fachang Inn in Weixiang Lane on Avenue Dubail and simultaneously swallowed raw opium to commit suicide. The next day at noon, the tea boy, Jin Guiyuan, noticed that Guo and his fiancée were still lying in bed. He knocked on the door but received no response. He climbed over the partition wall and saw that Guo was barely alive and Ms. Li was already dead. The inn reported the incident to the police, who sent detectives to transport Guo to Renji Hospital for treatment. A letter was found on his person detailing the events and flower gambling slips. Ms. Li's body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuantang for a post-mortem examination. As no relatives were found, the French Concession Police Criminal Division reported the case to Judge Zhu of the French Court. At 2:30 PM, Judge Zhu arrived at the morgue and confirmed that the deceased had committed suicide by poisoning. He ordered photographs to be taken and the court provided a coffin for the burial. It was reported that Guo died in the hospital at around 9:00 PM last night due to severe poisoning, despite attempts to save him.

Yu Qingyu's Appeal; Trial of Wu Jianguang et al. Opens

Judgment Scheduled for the 23rd

Wu Jianguang, Wang Yonghai, Wang Zhenhai, and the two sons of the deceased Chai Wenzhong, Cai Fa and Cai Gao, were previously sued by Kuomintang member Yu Qingyu for deceiving the public with superstitious talk and obtaining money through fraud. The Shanghai Special District Court concluded the trial and declared Wu and the others not guilty. This newspaper reported on this previously. Yu was not satisfied and appealed to the local court of the same court because it was a preliminary case. The court specially convened a collegial panel, headed by Judge Xu Jiashi and including Judges Ge and Sun. Wu and the two Wangs were brought to court and all claimed that they earned a living by fortune-telling. The Chai brothers stated that although their father was an astrologer, they had taken up other occupations since his death and that the two Wangs were their father's students, with no other relationship. Yu stated that he passed by Tibet Road and saw many astrology shops. Thinking that these people were dedicated to deceiving the public and should be punished, he entered Chai Wenzhong's fortune-telling shop, where Cai Fa greeted him. He told him that he wanted a fortune told, and Cai Fa said that he needed to pay a registration fee of six jiao first, which he paid. Cai Fa gave him a receipt. Wang Yonghai then told his fortune, and when Yu asked about a friend's illness, Yonghai said the divination was very ominous and that he needed to perform a ritual to ward off the bad luck, which would take two days and cost 176 yuan. He also gave him a bill. Wang Yonghai stated that because the divination was ominous, Yu asked if there was a way to resolve it. He replied that it was possible and asked Yu how much money he would need. He stated between forty to fifty yuan a day, totaling one hundred yuan for two days. Yu then asked him to add an introduction fee of sixty yuan and transportation costs of sixteen yuan to the bill, which is why the bill was for 176 yuan. Yu denied asking Yonghai to add an introduction fee and transportation costs. Wu Jianguang and the others then successively testified, and their statements were similar to those at the initial trial. After the testimony, the lawyers for both sides debated. The court ordered that a judgment be announced on the afternoon of the 23rd of this month.

Continued Hearing of the Case of the Murdered Daughter-in-Law of Constable Li Qingfu

Li and Chen's Statements Continued Yesterday

Li Qingfu Still Threatens People

Li Qingfu, a native of Anhui, was a Chinese constable No. 615 at the Gordon Road Police Station. He lived with his wife, Chen, his eldest son, Yu Long, and his second son, Yu Kun, at No. 660 Gordon Road. On the evening of the 27th of last month, they allegedly strangled his daughter-in-law, Zhang (Yu Long's wife), to death. The case was investigated by Chinese Detective Shao Jingfan of the police station, who arrested Li Qingfu and the other three and sent them to the Shanghai Special District Court. Except for Li Chen, who fainted in court during questioning and was sent to the hospital for treatment and therefore was not questioned, Li Qingfu and the other two had been questioned and ordered to be held for further investigation. This newspaper has reported on this three times previously. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi took his seat in the Second Criminal Court to continue the hearing. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the police stated that since the last court hearing, the police had conducted a detailed investigation and discovered new evidence. Since Zhang died suddenly in the middle of the night on August 27th, the third defendant, Li Yu Kun, went out on September 1st to look for a house to move into. He rented the remaining rooms of Zhou Wenhua's house at No. 87 Mingyuanfang, Huade Road, and paid a deposit of one yuan. The next day, Li Chen and Li Yu Long also went to see the house and moved two trunks there. The detectives opened the two trunks, one of which was empty and the other full of the deceased's clothes. Also, on September 5th, a train ticket was found on Yu Kun. This situation is suspicious. However, Zhou Wenhua, the second landlord of Huade Road, was asked to testify in court, but he did not arrive today. Detective Shao Jingfan complained that according to the defendant Li Qingfu, after his daughter-in-law died, he pawned her clothes the next day to prepare a coffin, but the pawnshop said that Li pawned the clothes on September 2nd, not on August 28th. Another point is that when the defendant Li Chen rented the house on Huade Road, she borrowed the living room from the second landlord and falsely claimed that her brother had recently died of illness and that the first seven days of mourning had passed and that she wanted to do the second seven days of mourning. The landlord agreed. This fact can be proven when the second landlord, Zhou Wenhua, arrives at court next time. The Judge Wu then questioned Li Chen, who stated that she lived at 666 Gordon Road with three families. Her daughter-in-law, Zhang, lived in the pavilion room upstairs. On the evening of the 27th of last month, at around 7:00 PM, she and her daughter-in-law had a quarrel during dinner, and she scolded her. After a neighbor persuaded them to reconcile, her daughter-in-law went upstairs to take a bath. She was cooling off at the door. About half an hour after she went to sleep, she heard a thud upstairs. She went upstairs to check and saw her daughter-in-law hanging herself on the door with a cloth she usually used to bind her feet. The thud was the sound of the small stool she was standing on when she hanged herself falling over. She quickly tried to save her and helped her onto the bed. At that time, she was still breathing but could not speak. She then massaged her. Her husband also heard the sound and asked what was happening upstairs. She falsely said that her daughter-in-law had a heatstroke. Her husband went out to look for someone to scrape her back and buy heatstroke medicine. After a while, she saw that her daughter-in-law's breath was getting shorter and she died at dawn. Because her daughter-in-law's suicide occurred after her quarrel with her, she was afraid of being blamed, so she claimed that she had heatstroke. This is the truth and there are no lies. Judge Wu asked her about the marks on the deceased's upper and lower teeth and two teeth fell out, and there was a purple-black mark under her tongue and a mark on her right shoulder and had marks, and if she claimed that her daughter-in-law had hanged herself, where did these injuries come from? She replied that she did not know and that she had never beaten her daughter-in-law before and asked for a clear judgment. Li Qingfu, Li Yu Long, Li Yu Kun, and the witness, Ms. Pan Wu, successively testified. Their testimonies were the same as the last time and have been reported in the newspaper, so they will not be repeated here. However, Ms. Pan Wu only stated that when the defendant Li Qingfu was detained in the waiting room today, he said to her through a small hole in the door that she should not incriminate him when she testified in court, implying a threat. She was very afraid because she was afraid that he would seek revenge on her after he was released from prison. Judge Wu reviewed the testimonies and, seeing that the witness Zhou Wenzhang had not arrived, ordered the four defendants to be detained separately and to continue the hearing on the afternoon of September 25.

Misfortunes Never Come Singly; Zhu Mintang Arrested

The Color Ticket Scheme of Guanghua Company

Zhu Mintang Involved in Criminal Case

Although Zhu Xiangjie, aka Zhu Mintang, has been personally negotiating with Zhao Xiuzhen in the case of inducing sexual relations by Zhao Xiuzhen, the result of repeated face-to-face negotiations to recover the spilled water and withdraw the private prosecution, the issue of lawyer's fees has been raised separately. After Zhang Chongding, a lawyer, repeatedly urged Zhao to fulfill his agreement to pay the attorney's fees, Zhao stated that although the matter had been settled amicably, the attorney's fees should be borne by Zhu. The two sides negotiated for several days until a compromise was reached for an attorney's fee of 300 yuan, but it had to be delayed for a few days. However, one wave was not over and another wave rose. The French Concession Guanghua Silver Company's criminal involvement in the color ticket matter involved Zhu Mintang. Zhu was taken away by detectives from the French police, and Zhu's family was running around trying to rescue him. At the same time, someone accused him of issuing a bad check from a certain bank for more than 1,070 yuan, which was returned upon maturity and unpaid. The French Court has reportedly issued a warrant for his arrest and detention.

Case of Unpaid Rent for Five Days

Hardoon Sues Guan Wuzhou

Judge Luo of the Seventh Court of the Special District Court recently heard a case of a foreign landlord oppressing a tenant. The lawyers for both sides debated for two hours. The audience paid close attention to the case. The houses at Nos. 243 and 244 Shandong Road, Block D, are the property of Hardoon Company and have been rented to Fan Tongsheng for the Guan Wuzhou Hat Shop for a monthly rent of 149 taels of silver, which has always been calculated according to the lunar calendar. Although the tenant requested that the calculation be changed to the solar calendar, the foreign company did not comply with current laws and regulations. Recently, the hat shop has been in a slump and has been closed for liquidation, and a takeover person has been found and a takeover price of 4,000 taels has been agreed upon, but it has not yet been completed. Unexpectedly, Hardoon Company posted a printed notice on the door of the house stating that the house was being taken back for rent, causing the takeover person to dare not take over. Hardoon Company's manager, Shen Licheng, sued in the Special District Court for two months of rent owed, totaling 298 taels of silver, claiming that it was rent owed for August and September according to the solar calendar. Judge Luo summoned the plaintiff and the defendant to court for a hearing. The plaintiff, Hardoon's manager Shen Licheng, arrived at court with lawyer Ye Fukang, and the defendant was fully represented by lawyer Zhu Xiyun. The plaintiff argued that he demanded to recover the rent for August and September and said that the posting of the rental notice was requested by the defendant. The defendant's lawyer argued that the plaintiff had always collected rent according to the lunar calendar and presented a letter from the plaintiff demanding rent for the leap June, which was sufficient to prove that it was undoubtedly the lunar calendar. Now, he is suing for rent owed for August and September to avoid violating the National Government's regulations that all rents should be calculated according to the solar calendar. However, if calculated according to the solar calendar, twenty-one days should be deducted, or at least nine days should be deducted. The plaintiff posted a rental notice on August 14, indicating that he would take back the house. According to this date, nine days should be deducted and only five days of rent are owed. Since the plaintiff posted a rental notice on the shop door, the defendant's already agreed-upon takeover had been canceled, causing significant losses (this matter will be reserved for further discussion). The landlord's oppression of the tenant forced the defendant to entrust the items in the shop to Yizhong Auction, but the plaintiff came out to stop him when he was removing the items. So he went to the General Police Station. The case has been accepted by the court and is awaiting court proceedings. The plaintiff's successive oppressions have forced the defendant to a dead end. The plaintiff's rent for August and September should be calculated according to the plaintiff's calculations for rent not yet lived in. How can he sue for it in advance? Today is the 15th, but the lawsuit was filed before the 15th. I am afraid there is no such reason in the world. Therefore, I request that the plaintiff's request be rejected. The plaintiff continued to say that the rent was paid in advance and there was a rent ticket stipulation. The defendant's lawyer said that this rent ticket was the standard of the landlord's oppression of the tenant. How could the tenant request a change? In short, he only owed five days of rent and wanted to sue for it. Is this not oppression? As a result, Judge Luo ordered an attempt at reconciliation. If it was unsuccessful, a judgment would be scheduled for a later date.

Red Pills More Harmful Than Opium

French Police Find Three More Cases

Because red pills are more harmful than opium, the French Concession authorities have instructed all detectives to strictly investigate and arrest those involved. The French police detectives recently discovered that Jiang Wenqing's house at No. 36 Deshan Lane on Avenue Dubail, the house of a woman named Chen Lao San at No. 28 in the same lane, and the house of Cao Wang at No. 183 Caishi Street, etc., had privately set up lighting to provide poor people to eat red pills inside and violated the prohibition, so they went to each place and seized the lighting and a number of red pills, brought them to the police station and ordered them to provide bail. Yesterday, they were summoned to the French Court to be investigated. First, the Western detective chief reported the previous situation and questioned the defendants, who admitted to privately selling red pills for people to eat under the lights. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced the three defendants to a fine of 200 yuan each and confiscated the items as a warning.

Lou Kenzai Kidnapping Case

Accomplice Du A'ge Apprehended

Lou Kenzai, the seventeen-year-old son of Lou Xunru, the president of the Qungong Bank, was studying at Qianye School on Peng Road. On the morning of November 4th last year, Kenzai was kidnapped by bandits on his way to school from his residence at No. 12 Mendelan Road. His family redeemed him for 10,000 yuan. Detective Wang Debiao of the Huishi Police Station arrested two kidnappers, Zhou Kui and Fan Xibo, who were interrogated and sentenced to death by shooting according to law. However, accomplice Du A'ge, also known as Du Pinxiang, from Tongzhou, escaped after the incident and disappeared. After an investigation, it was learned that the bandit was hiding in the house at No. 37 Kaifeng Road. The Chinese and Western detectives Zhu A'san, Wang Jinshou, and Wei Linsheng of the Huishi Police Station secretly went there and arrested Du on the afternoon of the previous day. Yesterday, he was sent to the Shanghai Special District Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi questioned him. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the police stated that the police still needed to investigate everything about the bandit and requested a postponement. Judge Wu questioned the bandit Du briefly and ordered him to be detained and rescheduled for another hearing.

Preventing Theft

Shops Must Pay Attention

Police Authorities' Opinion

Recently, there have been increasing reports of theft and impersonation of goods, which has attracted attention from all sectors. According to the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department, the police authorities alone are not enough to achieve results without the assistance of various shops. All shop owners and managers should be especially careful and pay attention when unfamiliar customers ask to be billed or claim that they will have the goods delivered to a certain place to collect the money. There are also thieves who take the opportunity to steal things during transactions. They go to the store pretending to buy goods, picking and choosing harshly, so that the shop assistants are distracted and unable to pay attention, and then use their skills to hide valuable items on their bodies and leave. Shop assistants should also pay attention to this situation at all times.

Start Planning The Process

The Municipal Charity Property Organization Committee held a founding ceremony at the Social Affairs Bureau at 2:00 PM on the 16th of this month. Present were: the city government representative Cen Dechang, secretary, City Party representative Comrade Xu Yefu, Charity representatives Chen Liangyu, and all the committee members. Labor Hospital

The Epidemic Department Continues to Provide Consultations and Medication as Usual

The Epidemic Has Not Been Eliminated and The End Date Postponed

Since its opening in early July, the Shanghai Labor Hospital Epidemic Department has provided countless consultations and medications. Because the epidemic has decreased the fifteenth of this month was the intended closing date, but since the beginning of autumn, more than ten cases of cholera have been discovered in the city. The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau sent a letter requesting this condition, as the department's duty is to provide relief to workers suffering from epidemics. Given that the bacteria has not been completely eliminated, the responsibility cannot be easily shirked. Department Director Li Runxiang, after consulting with Hospital Affairs Committee Chairman Pan Gongzhan and Vice Presidents Wang Jingyang and Wei Shouyuan, decided to postpone the closing date in order to better cope with the situation and maintain the health of the workers.

The Murder of the Chinese and Foreign Engineer Case

The Defendant Changed His Testimony at Yesterday's Trial

Witness Testimony Awaits Adjourned Trial

On May 30th of this year, Chinese and foreign engineers of the Dredging Bureau distributed wages on the Lifly steamer at Yangshupu when bandits robbed more than 2,000 yuan and shot and killed the engineers. The Xinzha Police Station arrested the defendants Zhang Gengshi, Feng Qing, and Yao Zucheng, and sent them to the Shanghai Local Court. The prosecutor filed a public prosecution. Yesterday, Judge Wu Zhen opened the court. The defendants all changed their testimonies, denying the claims and claiming that the testimonies they previously gave at the police station were obtained through torture. The judge then questioned Xu Zheng, A'zhang, and Shen A'jiang, who stated that they ran small motorboats at the Huangpu Steamboat Bureau. On that day, two people came to hire their boat and agreed on a fare of three yuan. They first sailed to the Taidong Wharf and stopped. Then eight or nine people came down. At that time, one of the people who hired the boat was Zhang Genfu, and Feng Qing was also among the people who later came to the boat, but Yao Zucheng was not seen. After about half an hour, they were ordered to sail to the Ruirong Shipyard in Yangshupu and then to the Huangpu Wharf. They went to the Lifly steamer. They ordered them to sail the two people on their ship to Qichang Warehouse in Pudong. The official said that he still needed to summon witnesses and ordered the defendants to be held for further trial.

Robbery on Tiantong Road

At around 9:00 PM on the previous evening, three robbers speaking with a Jiangbei accent broke into No. 5 Tiantong Road, Hongkou. All had handguns. One person stood guard at the door while two broke into the upstairs, forbidding anyone to make a sound, overturned boxes and cabinets, and searched at will. Gold jewelry and clothing were stolen, estimated to be worth about 796 yuan. The robbers left with the loot. The robbers fired a shot as they left, but fortunately no one was injured. The victim reported the incident to the police station and requested that they be apprehended.

Large Number of Refugees Passing Through Hongqiao Town

Three Hundred and Eighty Men, Women, and Children

At around 2:00 PM on the previous afternoon, three hundred and eighty refugees, men, women, and children from Xinhu, Hunan, led by Tan Zhiqin and Fang Yusheng, arrived at Hongqiao Town in western Shanghai from QibaTown, Songjiang. After arriving at the town, they extorted supplies from the local community. Fortunately, Pan Xuezeng, the chief of the Sixth District First Branch Police Station, learned of this and led the police to maintain order and guide them to settle down in nearby places such as the Anguo Temple Lianchang Temple, so the merchants did not suffer any losses. He immediately reported to the Beixinjing Town Sixth District First Branch Police Station. The head of the station, Wang Xixiang, and Inspector Li Cunzheng supervised the entire armed police force to suppress them and stated that this was the jurisdiction of the urban area and they were not allowed to stay here to avoid causing trouble. Then the Social Affairs Bureau sent personnel to allocate more than one hundred dollars, and yesterday morning the entire group set off to the northwest toward the Jiwang Temple.

Banning Russian Beggars

Ordering the Districts in the City to Immediately Expel Them

Recently, several Russian beggars have often appeared in front of the Small World gate in the city, forming gangs, dressed in rags, and with ferocious faces, blocking our young women and forcibly begging. The police on duty ignore them and do not interfere. Director Yuan of the Municipal Public Security Bureau was informed.

Page 16

Having learned that these Russian beggars had previously engaged in forcibly pulling passers-by and committing violence in the Qujiang Road area of Zhabei, an order had been issued to strictly ban them. Unexpectedly, they recently dared to run rampant in the downtown area, and the police did not stop them, allowing them to forcibly beg and extort money, which was extremely inappropriate. Yesterday, he strictly ordered the district offices in charge to instruct the police on duty to immediately expel these Russian beggars if they were encountered. Those who disobey will be detained and sent to Russian charitable organizations for care to avoid causing trouble and ensure public safety.

Large Quantities of Chinese Tea Transported to Russia

Two Thousand Five Hundred Tons

Since the resumption of Sino-Russian trade, several batches of Chinese tea have been transported to Russia. Yesterday, the Sino-Russian Assistance Society purchased more than 1 million yuan of Chinese tea for shipment to Russia, including 1,300 tons of green tea and 1,200 tons of brick tea.

Yao Guisheng Sues for Recovery of Debt

Defendant Hu Jingqing Given a Deadline to Settle

Yesterday, Yao Guisheng, through attorney Fei Xizhen, filed a lawsuit in the Criminal Division of the Public Concession Court against the defendant Hu Jingqing, alleging that the defendant had borrowed 3,000 yuan in silver from the plaintiff two years ago, with a promissory note. Of this amount, 1,000 yuan was guaranteed by a certain gentleman, and the remaining 2,000 yuan was secured by a Ford car, with an agreement to return the car upon repayment. However, the defendant repeatedly delayed and ignored the obligation. Furthermore, the car was repossessed by the car dealership due to the defendant's failure to pay the purchase price. The plaintiff contends that the defendant's actions constitute fraud and requests an investigation, prosecution, and appropriate punishment. Hu admitted to owing the money but claimed to be temporarily unable to repay it and requested an extension. Judge Zhu, presiding over the case, ordered the defendant to provide bail and settle the matter within seven days.

Bicycle races are highly stimulating and interesting. Spectators feel refreshed and invigorated. The most noteworthy of these are: (1) The international race between the Chinese, Japanese, and An teams, with two top athletes from each country competing; (2) a forty-lap paced race; (3) a grand performance by world-class experts on motorized bicycles; (4) the finals of the Pengsheng Plank twenty-lap race. Two Fires Last Night

Xiqipan Street: At approximately 7:30 PM last night, a large box of unopened tins of fire liquor (likely a flammable solvent) was stored at Chengchangxiang Paint Shop, number 6, Xiqipan Street, Wuma Road. A fire was accidentally ignited by apprentice playful behavior nearby, causing the fire to spread rapidly and engulf the roof. Another apprentice, Cai Ayu, an eighteen-year-old native of Ningbo, suffered severe burns, resulting in a charred and unrecognizable appearance. He was taken by ambulance to Renji Hospital for treatment. One house was destroyed in the fire.

Huaji Road: At 8:04 PM last night, a fire broke out on the upper floor of Zhang Renhe's grocery store, number 711, Huaji Road, Hongkou, due to apparent carelessness. The fire quickly engulfed the roof and spread to the adjacent Zaopi shed of Dafengyong Cigarette and Paper Shop at number 712. Firefighters from the fire department rushed to the scene to extinguish the flames. A total of two houses were destroyed.

Dr. R.W. Paul, director of the Shanghai Sanatorium and Hospital's city department located at 33 Laobazi Road, has returned to Shanghai after a trip to the United States. He will continue to practice at the Laobazi Road branch. It is also reported that the hospital's president, Dr. H.W. Miller, will arrive in Shanghai today and will resume practicing at the Luobiegen Road clinic in the Western District.

Dongjiadu Vegetable Market Soon to be Built

The southern part of Shanghai has long lacked a proper vegetable market, with vegetable stalls scattered along the streets, causing significant traffic congestion. The Municipal Bureau of Public Works has long considered converting the old municipal buildings in Dongjiadu into a vegetable market, but the project has been delayed due to funding issues. It is now reported that the municipal government has secured funding for the project, and the Bureau of Public Works is conducting bidding. Construction is expected to begin soon, which will greatly benefit residents in the southern part of Shanghai.

Zhabei Unions: Declaration regarding the Tiancheng Silk Weaving Factory's suspension of raw material supply, hindering work: The Tiancheng Silk Weaving Factory, while strengthening union efforts to develop production, is forcibly reducing wages, suspending the supply of raw materials, and dismantling machinery, cutting off workers' livelihoods. Our unions have repeatedly received appeals for assistance from Tiancheng Union representatives and must provide sympathetic support. Since its establishment in 1925, Tiancheng Factory has grown from eight to forty-five machines, with annual profits reaching hundreds of thousands of yuan. Its rayon fabrics can be said to be at their peak today. However, the factory is not considering production progress and is forcibly reducing workers' wages and suspending the supply of raw materials, making it impossible for workers to work. It is also dismantling machinery and adding hundreds of foreign machines, causing the factory's workers no peace. The factory's wages are based on piecework, with a price of 42 cents per foot. Now the factory is forcing the union to reduce this to 28 cents, while the workers are willing to reduce it to 38 cents. After arbitration by the authorities, the price was set at 33 cents, but the factory has since suspended the supply of raw materials, dismantled machinery, and added foreign machines to implement a wage reduction plan. Fortunately, the workers have recognized the factory's scheme and have collectively resisted its implementation. Given the actions of the Tiancheng Factory's management, our unions, as part of the same front, deeply hate the factory's authorities. In addition to jointly submitting a petition to the Party and government authorities for prompt action and being willing to support the Tiancheng Union, we urge all Shanghai workers to pay attention to prevent other factories from imitating these actions. This declaration is jointly issued by the Shanghai Commercial Press Union, the Huayang Printing Union, the Huashang Public Bus Workers' Union, the Huazhuang Binding Zhabei District Union, the Jingyi Niushang Leather Factory Union, the Western Clothing Union, the Tea Box Union, the General Affairs Office Staff Union, the Zhabei Cleaning Workers' Union, the Coal and Wood Workers' Union, the British-owned Zilai Yanxing Union, the Wenwei Union, the Huayang Cloth Industry Staff Union, the Lithographic Gum Paper Union, the Bristle Union, the Tea Processing Union, the Zhufeng Union, the Eighth Silk Factory Business Union, and others.

To the Editor:

In this morning's edition of your newspaper, under the local news section, an article titled "Wife of a Sailor" mentions "[actually took a fancy to Hu Yongkang, who was selling Jakelin medicine on the road]". After investigation, Hu Yongkang is not an employee of our company, nor is he a seller of Jakelin medicine. Even if he were selling Jakelin medicine, it would certainly be counterfeit medicine, as such counterfeit medicines are rampant in the market. Therefore, we kindly request a correction.

Sincerely,

Henry White Pharmaceutical Company

Shanghai Market

Business News

The Du Jinsheng General Store on North Sichuan Road announces that the art samples published by the factory have been highly praised by people at home and abroad since they were distributed as gifts last year, hailed as the finest silk gifts of domestic origin. Therefore, the previous two editions have been exhausted. Now, the third edition, commemorating the wedding of the Dalai couple, is already printed. This is a photograph commemorating the 56th wedding anniversary of the Dalai couple.

It has also been printed and will be distributed to all circles starting today. The content is even more exquisite. The book is 32mo, about dozens of pages, printed on 100-pound coated paper with more than 200 copperplate prints. The cover is a three-color plate printed with the Hall of Prayer for Good Harvests in Beijing, which is also a product of this factory. The factory has made a great sacrifice in this promotion. To promote domestic products, those who need to send a letter should attach a postal fee of 15 cents and can receive a copy.

Youth Land

Impressions of a Northern Journey (1)

— Su Ling

Traveling North in Flying Snow

The tender light of the winter morning caresses Shanghai, still asleep. Our car, splashing the snow accumulated last night, speeds past the bustling workers and heads towards the river. In that instant, I bid farewell to Shanghai.

Having been tossed around by fate for years, this journey north is also at the mercy of fate. Although I am not one to succumb to fate.

Almost a month ago, I received two letters summoning me to the north. Due to past hunger, suffering, and unfortunate circumstances, even though I am about to drift to the far outside the pass, and that area is close to the terrifying Sino-Russian War zone, I have made this decision to brave danger and embark on a long journey for the sake of hope and longing.

Later, the biggest reason that prevented me from going from Shanghai to Harbin was the 100 yuan needed for travel expenses. I could not find a way to raise this terrible amount.

I thought I could not realize the northern journey. I went to Nanjing to look for a job, but a airmail letter drove me back to Shanghai again. It turned out that a friend who was returning north invited me to travel with him and lent me travel expenses.

It seems that fate has destined me. I am fighting against fate.

Ling, you should go to the north. This is a great opportunity for you to create for yourself. You must not miss this opportunity. Your continuous sorrow in the south has caused great losses to you..."" my friends told me.

Yes, I am thinking like that and determined to go north. Although I can't predict what the phenomenon will be after going north, it is a very happy thing that I can get a chance to travel this time. There are black forests and empty deserts in the north. The mountains are permanently white, and snow is flying in the sky all year round... These will give my soul infinite great feelings, and there, I can better than in the south. Closer opportunities to observe the red Russ rampant looting and all brutal circumstances on our nation..."

This time, I am on the road of the Long March. When people spend this shivering end of winter around the stove, I am marching to the cold zone and to the north where the snow is flying all year round.

I left Xie Jun and Luo Jun's hands silently and stood on the sampan. After another humming gong, the engine started to sound and the ship body gradually left the dock.

Wandering in the Embrace of Nature

— Hua She

Goodbye Shanghai, goodbye the friends at the Bund, goodbye...

The crowd on the dock gradually blurred in my sight. Shanghai gradually left him far away. I pulled Chen Jun (a friend who was traveling with me) and walked back to the cabin silently, gazing at the two pieces that had been with me in the south for several years. Lived in broken luggage.

The expedition began. I want to take you to the outside of the Great Wall, where there are no fallen peach petals that have been blown by the south wind will fall on your back. There is snow flying all year round.

Youth Land Submission Guidelines

(1) Articles should discuss youth issues, domestic and foreign school or student news, essays, school life descriptions, essays, etc. The scope and style are not limited.

(2) Books are limited to those concerning youth issues.

(3) Photos should be qualified for youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, drama, speech, assembly, exhibition, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements. All individuals and groups are welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

(6) Do not fix the manuscript horizontally, and do not write carelessly. Western text can be omitted if possible. If the original text must be cited, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black paint.

(8) Please indicate on the submitted manuscript that it is to be received by the Youth Land Editorial Department.

(9) Whether the submitted manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Compensation for articles is divided into three types: 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words. The compensation for pictures and photos is the same as above for each picture. If there are special manuscripts, the compensation will be calculated separately.
